Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Condition of Intention for Muhadhat to Invalidate Prayer
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a woman's muhadhat invalidates the imam's prayer and explain why intention is required.

Core Idea
Muhadhat invalidates the imam's prayer only if he intended the woman's imamate.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author explains a key nuance: a woman standing in line with the imam does not automatically invalidate his prayer. It depends on the imam's intention. This ruling protects the imam from unintended invalidation and is rooted in the principle that ishtirak (association) requires commitment (iltizam). We will unpack the ruling, the proofs, and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (muhadhat by a woman) and what the ruling is (imam's prayer invalidated only if he intended her imamate).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith 'akhkhiruhunna' which imposes a duty on the imam to arrange followers, and the principle of iltizam (commitment) which requires intention for that duty to be effective.
3
Understand the Hanafi position on ishtirak
The Hanafi school holds that ishtirak (association between imam and follower) requires intention. Without it, the woman does not become a follower, so her presence does not affect the imam's prayer.
Contrary to Zufar who does not require intention.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Zufar
Zufar argues that mere joining creates ishtirak. The Hanafi response is that ishtirak is based on commitment, which is actualized by intention.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if the imam did not intend, his prayer is valid; Zufar says both are invalid.
5
Evaluate the two scenarios when woman stands behind
When the woman is behind and there is no man beside her, there are two narrations: one requires intention (due to potential muhadhat), the other does not. The relied-upon view is that intention is not required in this case.
The difference is actual vs. potential invalidation.

وانما يشترط نية الامامة اذا ايتمت محاذية وان يكن يجنبها رجل ففيه روايتان والفرق على احدهما ان الفساد في الاول لازم وفى الثانى محتس
ترجمہ اور اگر امام نے عورت کا امام ہونے کی نیت نہیں کی تو عورت کی محاذات مرد کے لئے مضر نہ ہوگی اور عورت کی نماز جائز نہ ہوں اور اگر عورت کیونکہ اشتراک بغیر امامت کی نیت کے ہمارے نزدیک ثابت نہ ہوگا، بر خلاف قول زفر کے کیا تم نہیں دیکھتے کہ امام پر لازم ہے ترتیب کرنا امام کے لئے۔ بر ایک کے کھڑے ہونے کے مقام کا تو یہ بات امام کے لازم کرنے پر موقوف رہے گی۔ جیسے اقتداء کا حال ہے اور امامت کی نیت ان محاذی نہیں ہے لہند وقت شرط ہے جب کہ عورت نے محاذی ہو کر اقتداء کی ہو اور اگر عورت کے پہلو میں کوئی مرد نہ ہو تو اس میں دور و استیں ہیں۔ اور فرق کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو دونوں روایتوں میں سے ایک پر یہ ہے کہ فساد نماز اول میں لازم ہے اور دوسری صورت میں فساد کا احتمال ہے۔

پھر واضح ہو کہ مرد کا اس امام مرد کی اقتداء کرنا بغیر نیت امامت کے صحیح ہے یعنی اگر امام نے یہ نیت نہیں کی کہ میں اس کا امام ہوں تب بھی مرد اس امام کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے پس اسی طرح بغیر نیت امامت کے عورت کا اقتداء کرنا بھی صحیح ہوگا پس ثابت ہوا کہ مرد کی نماز کے فساد کے لئے عورت کے امام ہونے کی نیت کرنا شرط نہیں ہے۔ لیکن ہمارے نزدیک بغیر امام کے اشتراک ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حدیث اخر وهن" کی وجہ سے مقتدیوں کو بالترتیب کھڑا کرنے کی ذمہ داری امام پر ہے یعنی ترتیب مقام امام پر لازم ہے اور جس شخص پر کوئی چیز لازم ہو وہ اس کے لازم کرنے پر موقوف ہوتی ہے یعنی اگر لازم کرے گا تو لازم ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔ جیسے اقتداء کا حال ہے کہ مندی کا اقتداء کرنے کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے اس لئے کہ اس نیت اقتداء سے وہ اپنی نماز کو امام کی منمانت میں دے گا تا کہ امام کی کسی حرکت سے نماز میں نقص و ضرر پیدا ہو تو مقتدی کے قبول کرنے اور اس کی رضامندی سے اس پر لازم آئے۔ اس طرح امام کا عورتوں کی امامت کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے تاکہ عورتوں کی جانب سے اگر کوئی ضرر ہوتو وہ امام کا قبول کیا ہوا ہو۔ شمس الائمہ السرخسی نے بغیر نیت امامت کے امام کی نمائے گا مد نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ بیان کی ہے کہ اگر بغیر نیت امامت کے عورت کی اقتدا هیچ قرار دیدی جائے تو ہر عورت من چاہے طریقہ پر مرد کی نماز فاسد کر دینے پر قادر ہوگی اس طرح پر کہ مرد کی اقتداء کر کے ان کے پہلو میں کھڑی ہو جائے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں مرد کا ضرر ہے اس وجہ سے مرد کے لئے نیت امامت کو شرط قرار دیا گیا تا کہ یہ ضر ر مرد کی رضامندی سے اس پر لازم آئے۔

وانما يشترط نية الامامة، یہاں سے صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام کا امامت کی نیت کرتا اسی وقت شرط ہے جب کہ عورت امام کی ناز یہ ہوکر اس کی مقتدی بنے، یعنی محاذات کی وجہ سے امام کی نماز جب ہی فاسد ہوگی جبکہ عورت نے اس کے محاذ کی ہو کر اقتداء کی ہو اور امام نے اس کی امامت کی بھی نیت کی ہو اور اگر عورت امام کے پیچھے کھڑی ہوئی تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ یہ عورت کسی مرد مقتدی سے کافی بن کر کھڑی ہوئی۔ دوم یہ کہ کسی مرد مقتدی کے محاذی بن کر کھڑی نہیں ہوئی۔ یعنی اس کے پہلو میں کوئی مرد نہیں ہے۔ اگر یہ عورت مرد مقتدی کے محاذی ہو کر کھڑی ہوئی تو صحیح یہ ہے کہ بغیر امامت کی نیت یہ عورت مقتد یہ نہیں ہوگی۔
اور اگر عورت کے پہلو میں کوئی مرد نہ ہو یعنی اس کا محاذی کوئی مرد نہ ہو تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت میں امامت کی نیت کہنا نام کے لئے شرط ہے اور ایک روایت میں شرط نہیں ہے۔ دونوں رواتیوں کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بالفصل تو عورت کاری نہیں ہے لہذا اس کی ذات سے کوئی فساد بھی نہیں ہے البتہ اس بات کا احتمال ہے کہ وہ آگے بڑھ کر محاذ یہ ہو جائے پس اگر اس احتمال کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو نیت امامت شرط ہو گی تا کہ فساد نماز اس کے التزام کرنے سے ہو اور اگر یہ احتمال ملحوظ نہ ہو تو نیت شرط نہیں ہوگی۔ رہی یہ بات کہ ان دونوں روایتوں میں سے نیت شرط ہونے کی روایت اور اول صورت میں کیا فرق ہے تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ اول صورت میں یعنی جب کہ عورت کسی مرد کے محاذی کھڑی ہوئی ہو فساد بالفعل واقع ہے اور دوسری صورت میں فساد کا امکان ہے یعنی جب کہ عورت امام کے پیچھے کھڑی ہوئی اور اس کے پہلو میں کوئی مرد نہ ہو۔ تو اس صورت میں فساد کا احتمال ہے کہ وہ آگے بڑھ کر مرد کے گاؤ کی ہو جائے پس اس احتمال کو واقع پر قیاس کر کے نیت شرط کی گئی حتی کہ اگر اعتبار نہ کریں تو نیت شرط نہیں۔ جیسا کہ دوسری روایت ہے۔
And intention of imamate is only required when a woman follows as a muqtadiyah while being in line (muhadhat). And if there is no man beside her, then there are two narrations. The difference between them is that in the first, the invalidation is necessary, and in the second, it is potential.
Translation: If the imam did not intend to be the imam for the woman, then her muhadhat does not harm the man, and her prayer is not valid. Because according to us, association (ishtirak) is not established without the intention of imamate, contrary to Zufar's view. Don't you see that the imam is obligated to arrange the positions of followers? This obligation depends on his commitment (iltizam). Like the case of iqtida: the follower must intend to follow. Similarly, intention of imamate is a condition only when the woman follows while in line. And if there is no man beside the woman, there are two narrations. In one, intention is a condition; in the other, it is not. The reason: in this case, there is no actual muhadhat, so no invalidation, but there is a possibility that she may move forward and become in line. If this possibility is considered, intention is required so that invalidation occurs by his commitment; if not, intention is not required.

Then it becomes clear that a man can follow an imam without the imam intending to lead him. Similarly, a woman may follow without intention. So the invalidation of the man's prayer does not depend on the imam's intention for the woman. However, according to us, ishtirak (association) is not established without intention. The reason is that the hadith 'akhkhiruhunna' places the duty of arranging followers on the imam. This duty depends on his commitment. Just as in iqtida, the follower's intention is necessary to accept potential harm. Similarly, the imam's intention for the woman is required so that any harm from her side is accepted by him. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi explained that without intention, if a woman's following were considered valid, any woman could invalidate a man's prayer by standing beside him, which would be harmful. So intention is made a condition to ensure that harm is accepted by his consent.

'And intention of imamate is only required' - here the author of Hidayah says that the imam's intention is a condition only when the woman follows while being in line (muhadhat). The imam's prayer is invalidated only if she follows in line and he intended her imamate. If the woman stands behind the imam, there are two scenarios: first, she stands in line with a male follower; second, she does not stand in line with any male follower (i.e., no man beside her). If she stands in line with a male follower, the correct view is that without intention of imamate, she does not become a follower. If there is no man beside her, there are two narrations: one requires intention, the other does not. The basis: in this case, there is no actual muhadhat, so no invalidation, but there is a possibility that she may move forward and become in line. If that possibility is considered, intention is required so that invalidation is by his commitment; if not, intention is not required. The difference between the narration requiring intention and the first scenario: in the first scenario (woman in line with a man), invalidation is actual; in the second scenario (woman behind without a man beside), invalidation is potential. So analogy with the actual case requires intention if the possibility is considered; otherwise not, as in the second narration.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage expands on the condition of intention (niyyah) for the invalidation caused by muhadhat. The author explains that if a woman stands in line with the imam (or a male follower), the imam's prayer is invalidated only if he had the intention to be her imam. Without his intention, her prayer is invalid (she does not become a follower), but his prayer remains valid. This is based on the principle that ishtirak (partnership in the prayer) requires intention, unlike the view of Imam Zufar. The duty of arranging followers is incumbent upon the imam, but this duty becomes effective only when he commits to it by intention, similar to how a follower must intend to follow to accept any potential harm. Sarakhsi adds a rationale: without the condition of intention, any woman could maliciously invalidate a man's prayer by joining and standing in line, so intention ensures that any harm is voluntarily accepted by the imam.

The passage then details two scenarios when a woman stands behind the imam (not in line): (1) if she stands in line with a male follower, intention is required for her to be considered a follower; (2) if there is no man beside her, there are two narrations: one requires intention (considering the possibility of her moving forward to become in line), and the other does not. The difference is that in the first scenario invalidation is actual, while in the second it is potential.

Key Terms
اشتراك (ishtirāk): Partnership in the prayer, meaning the woman becomes a follower of the imam and thus subject to the same rulings.
التزام (iltizām): Commitment; the imam's acceptance of the responsibility for the woman's presence in his prayer, actualized by intending her imamate.
مقتدی (muqtadī): A follower in prayer; here used specifically for a female follower (muqtadiyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rationale behind requiring the imam's intention for a woman's muhadhat to invalidate his prayer?
A) The hadith 'akhkhiruhunna' directly orders it.
B) To protect the imam from unintended invalidation by ensuring he commits to the woman's presence.
C) Because women are not allowed to pray behind men without intention.
D) To make the woman's prayer valid.

Key Takeaway
The imam's intention is a necessary condition for a woman's muhadhat to invalidate his prayer; without it, his prayer remains valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Imam's Intention for Women: When is it Required?
Explains when imam's niyyah for leading women is required due to muhadhat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scenarios for the imam's intention and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on actual vs potential corruption.

Core Idea
Imam's intention required only when woman is parallel; otherwise it's not a condition.

In Hanafi fiqh, the imam's intention to lead women is not always required. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that it becomes a condition only when the woman is parallel (muhādhi) to the imam or to a male follower. The reasoning hinges on whether actual corruption exists or only a potential one. Understanding this distinction protects the validity of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The author states that the imam's intention to lead women is a condition only when the woman is parallel to the imam. However, there are additional sub-scenarios when the woman stands behind the imam.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the woman's position and whether she is parallel to any male.
2
Analyze the scenarios
When the woman stands behind the imam, two forms exist: (1) she stands parallel to a male follower, and (2) she stands with no man beside her. In form (1), intention is required because actual corruption occurs. In form (2), there are two narrations due to potential corruption.
The difference between the two forms is whether corruption is actual or merely potential.
3
Trace the reasoning (talil)
Actual corruption necessitates the imam's intention to attribute the corruption to his consent. Potential corruption is analogized (qiyas) to actual corruption by some narrations, making intention a condition as a precaution. Other narrations disregard the potential and do not require intention.
This is an example of qiyas from actual to potential harm, a common Hanafi istihsan-based reasoning.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
When the woman is behind with no man beside her, there are two authentic narrations: one requiring intention (mu'tamad) and one not. The author sides with the narration requiring intention.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that intention is required in this case as well, to avoid the risk of corruption.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a woman is parallel to the imam or to a male follower, the imam must intend to lead her; otherwise her following is invalid. If she is behind with no man beside, the imam should still intend to lead her according to the preferred view.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that in the second scenario, some Hanafi imams may not require intention, but caution dictates it.

Source Text

وانما يشترط نية الامامة، يہاں سے صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام کا امامت کی نیت کرنا اسی وقت شرط ہے جب کہ عورت امام کی محاذی ہوکر اس کی مقتدی بنے ، یعنی محاذات کی وجہ سے امام کی نماز جب ہی فاسد ہوگی جبکہ عورت نے اس کے محاذی ہو کر اقتداء کی ہو اور امام نے اس کی امامت کی بھی نیت کی ہو اور اگر عورت امام کے پیچھے کھڑی ہوئی تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ یہ عورت کسی مرد مقتدی سے محاذی بن کر کھڑی ہوئی۔ دوم یہ کہ کسی مرد مقتدی کے محاذی بن کر کھڑی نہیں ہوئی ۔ یعنی اس کے پہلو میں کوئی مرد نہیں ہے۔ اگر یہ عورت مرد مقتدی کے محاذی ہو کر کھڑی ہوئی تو صحیح یہ ہے کہ بغیر امامت کی نیت یہ عورت مقتدیہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اگر عورت کے پہلو میں کوئی مرد نہ ہو یعنی اس کا محاذی کوئی مرد نہ ہو تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت میں امامت کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے اور ایک روایت میں شرط نہیں ہے۔ دونوں روایتوں کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بالفعل تو عورت محاذی نہیں ہے لہذا اس کی ذات سے کوئی فساد بھی نہیں ہے البتہ اس بات کا احتمال ہے کہ وہ آگے بڑھ کر محاذیہ ہو جائے پس اگر اس احتمال کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو نیت امامت شرط ہو گی تا کہ فساد نماز اس کے التزام کرنے سے ہو اور اگر یہ احتمال ملحوظ نہ ہو تو نیت شرط نہیں ہوگی ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ ان دونوں روایتوں میں سے نیت شرط ہونے کی روایت اور اول صورت میں کیا فرق ہے تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ اول صورت میں یعنی جب کہ عورت کسی مرد کے محاذی کھڑی ہوئی ہو فساد بالفعل واقع ہے اور دوسری صورت میں فساد کا امکان ہے یعنی جب کہ عورت امام کے پیچھے کھڑی ہوئی اور اس کے پہلو میں کوئی مرد نہ ہو۔ تو اس صورت میں فساد کا احتمال ہے کہ وہ آگے بڑھ کر مرد کے محاذی ہو جائے پس اس احتمال کو واقع پر قیاس کر کے نیت شرط کی گئی حتی کہ اگر اعتبار نہ کریں تو نیت شرط نہیں ۔ جیسا کہ دوسری روایت ہے۔ (ي)
And the condition of intention of imamah: From here the author of Hidayah said that the imam's intention of imamah is a condition only when the woman is parallel to the imam and follows him, that is, due to parallelism the imam's prayer will become invalid only when the woman has followed him while being parallel to him and the imam has also intended her imamah. And if the woman stands behind the imam, there are two forms: first, that this woman stands parallel to some male follower; second, that she does not stand parallel to any male follower, i.e., there is no man beside her. If this woman stands parallel to a male follower, then the correct view is that without the intention of imamah this woman will not be a follower. And if there is no man beside the woman, i.e., no man is parallel to her, then there are two narrations. In one narration, intention of imamah is a condition, and in one narration it is not a condition. The reason for both narrations is that in this situation she is not actually parallel, so there is no corruption from her person, but there is a possibility that she may step forward and become parallel. So if this possibility is considered, then intention of imamah is a condition so that corruption of prayer occurs by her undertaking it; and if this possibility is not considered, then intention is not a condition. As for the difference between the narration where intention is a condition and the first situation, the answer is that in the first situation, i.e., when the woman stands parallel to a man, corruption is actual; and in the second situation, corruption is potential, i.e., when the woman stands behind the imam and there is no man beside her. In this situation, there is a possibility that she may step forward and become parallel to the man. So by analogizing this possibility to the actual case, intention is made a condition; if we do not consider it, intention is not a condition, as in the second narration.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussion about the condition of the imam's intention (niyyah) for leading women in congregational prayer. The author of Al-Hidayah, Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, states that the imam's intention to lead women is only required when the woman is parallel (muhādhi) to the imam, i.e., standing directly beside or in line with him, because this causes corruption of the prayer due to close proximity of a woman to the imam. The passage then explains that if the woman stands behind the imam, there are two scenarios. First, if she stands parallel to a male follower (i.e., beside a man), then without the imam's intention, she cannot validly follow, because the presence of a woman in line with a man corrupts his prayer. Second, if she stands behind the imam with no man beside her, there are two narrations: one requiring intention and one not. The reasoning is that in this case, she is not actually parallel, so no actual corruption exists; however, there is a possibility she might step forward and become parallel. If we consider this possibility, intention is required so that the corruption only occurs if the imam accepts it by his intention. If we ignore this possibility, intention is not required. The difference between the first scenario (woman parallel to man) and the second narration (woman behind but possibility) is that in the first, corruption is actual (bāz̤il), while in the second, it is merely potential. Thus, in the first case, intention is required; in the second, it is not, according to one narration. This reflects the Hanafi principle of considering both actual and potential harm in acts of worship.

Key Terms
نية الإمامة (niyyat al-imāmah): The imam's intention to lead the prayer for specific followers, in this case women.
محاذاة (muḥādhāt): The alignment or parallelism of a woman with the imam or male follower, causing corruption of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which situation is the imam's intention a condition for the validity of the woman's following, according to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the passage?
A) Only when the woman is parallel to the imam
B) When the woman is parallel to the imam or to a male follower
C) When the woman is behind the imam with a man beside her
D) In all situations, regardless of her position

Key Takeaway
The imam's intention to lead women is a condition only when actual or potential corruption from parallelism exists; otherwise it is not required.

Conditions of Muhadhat That Invalidate Prayer
Listing conditions of muhadhat with proof from nas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions of muhadhat that invalidate the man's prayer and explain their proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Muhadhat invalidates a man's prayer only when four specific conditions from the text are met — not by mere proximity.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, Imam al-Marghinani enumerates the conditions under which a woman's alignment (muhadhat) with a man during prayer corrupts the man's prayer. This ruling is a departure from qiyas, so it is limited to the conditions explicitly mentioned in the textual evidence. We will unpack each condition and examine the hadith proof that supports them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the alignment (muhadhat) of a woman with a man during prayer. The ruling is that it invalidates the man's prayer (makes it fasid) if all conditions are met. The act itself is makruh tahrimi.
The ruling is contrary to qiyas, so it is restricted to the text.
2
List the four conditions
The passage states four conditions: shared prayer (in tahrima and ada), absolute prayer (includes ruku and sujud), the woman is ahl al-shahwa (desirable), and no barrier between them.
Each condition is essential; missing any one prevents invalidation.
3
Examine the application through the masbuq scenario
The commentator illustrates with a scenario: a man and woman are masbuq (join late), then leave for wudu, return, and she aligns with him. The alignment only invalidates in the rak'ats that are shared in both tahrima and ada.
This clarifies the first condition: sharing must be in both takbir and performance.
4
Locate the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The proof is a hadith narrated by Aisha: 'O people, forbid your women from wearing adornment and walking proudly in the mosques, for the Children of Israel were not cursed until their women did so.' The command 'anhawa' indicates prohibition, and the analogy to Bani Israel shows the severity.
The dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and zanni al-dalala, but sufficient for a ruling contrary to qiyas.
5
Note the critical response
The Sahib 'Inaya (author of al-'Inaya) rejected this proof because the hadith does not mention prayer or alignment. Hanafi scholars responded that the ruling is based on the general prohibition of fitna, and the conditions are derived from the text and ijtihad.
This shows the scholarly debate around the evidence.

Source Text

ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جس کو ابن عبدالبر نے اپنی سند کے ساتھ حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا سے روایت کیا ہے ايها الناس انهوا نساء كم عن لبس الزينته والتبختر فى المساجدفان بني اسرائيل لم يلعنوا حتى لبست نساء هم الزينته وتنجتر و افي المساجد یعنی اے لوگو! اپنی عورتوں کو مسجدوں میں زینت اور تکبر کا لباس پہنے سے منع کرو کیونکہ بنواسرائیل ملعون نہیں ہوئے یہاں تک کہ ان کی عورتوں نے مساجد میں زینت اور فخر و غرور کا لباس پہنا چونکہ ہمارے اس زمانے میں فراق کا غلبہ ہے اس لئے غیر مزین عورتوں کو بھی منع کیا گیا ہے۔
چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ دونوں کے درمیان کوئی چیز حائل نہ ہو مثلا ستون یا کوئی اور چیز یا اتنی جگہ خالی ہو کہ اس میں ایک مرد کھڑ ا ہو جائے۔ ان مذکورہ شرطوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ محاذات کا مقصد نماز ہونا خلاف قیاس نص یعنی اخر وهن من حيث اخر من الله سے معلوم ہوا ہے بذا ان تمام امور کی رعایت رکھی جائے گی جن کے ساتھ نص وارد ہوئی۔ صاحب عنا یہ نے اس استدلال کو مسترد کیا ہے چنانچہ فر مایا کہ اس حدیث میں نماز ہی کا ذکر نہیں چہ جائے کہ ان قیود کا ذکر ہولیکن نفی حضرات نے ان قیود کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے بڑے تکلفات سے کام لیا ہے اس کے لئے علامہ الہند مولانا عبدالحئی کا حاشیہ ماید ملاحظہ کیجئے۔
The conditions of muhadhat (alignment) are: the prayer must be shared (in takbir and performance), the prayer must be absolute (with ruku and sujud), the woman must be one who is desired (ahl al-shahwa), and there must be no barrier between them. Because muhadhat's corruption is known by text contrary to analogy, so all conditions mentioned in the text are observed. [Commentary in Urdu follows, explaining each condition and its application, including a case where a man and woman are masbuq and the effect on muhadhat. The proof is from the hadith: 'O people, forbid your women from wearing adornment and walking proudly in the mosques, for the Children of Israel were not cursed until their women wore adornment and walked proudly in the mosques.']
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the conditions under which the alignment (muhadhat) of a woman with a man during prayer invalidates the man's prayer. The author lists four conditions from the authoritative text (nas). The ruling is a departure from qiyas (analogy), so all the conditions mentioned in the nas must be exactly observed. The first condition is that the prayers must be shared in both the opening takbir (tahrima) and the performance (ada). This means both persons must be praying the same prayer under the same imam in spirit, or one is imam and the other follower, or both are followers of a single imam. The second condition is that the prayer is absolute, i.e., includes ruku and sujud, not janaza prayer. The third condition is that the woman is one who is potentially desirable (ahl al-shahwa), free or slave, whether related or not. The fourth condition is that there is no barrier (hail) between them, such as a pillar or enough space for a man to stand. The proof is a hadith about the women of Bani Israel, though some scholars like Sahib 'Inaya criticized this evidence. The commentary then elaborates on each condition with examples, such as a case where a man and woman both join the imam late, then leave for wudu, return and she aligns with him. The alignment invalidates the man's prayer only in the shared rak'ats where both conditions of sharing exist. The author emphasizes that since the ruling is contrary to qiyas, it is restricted to what the text explicitly specifies.

Key Terms
محاذاة (muhadhat): alignment in prayer where a woman stands parallel to a man within the same row, potentially invalidating the man's prayer under certain conditions.
حائل (hail): a physical barrier such as a pillar or enough space for a man that prevents the alignment from being direct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The woman must be ahl al-shahwa (desirable).
B) The prayer must be janaza prayer.
C) The prayer must be shared in tahrima and ada.
D) There must be no barrier between them.

Key Takeaway
The alignment of a woman with a man during prayer only invalidates the man's prayer when all four conditions are met: shared prayer, absolute prayer, woman is ahl al-shahwa, and no barrier.

Women Attending Congregational Prayers: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on young and old women attending mosque congregations and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Young women are discouraged from mosques due to fitna; old women may attend but with restrictions.

The question of women attending congregational prayers in the mosque has been debated among the schools of fiqh. The Hanafi school takes a cautious approach, distinguishing between young and old women. This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling, its proof, and responds to the Shafi'i position. We will examine the legal reasoning and the key evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Find the explicit hukm for women attending congregational prayers. Note that it differentiates between young women (shawab) and old women (ajuz).
The ruling for young women is makruh tahrimi; for old women it is permissible with a restriction according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Extract the Hanafi proofs
List the proofs cited: (1) fear of fitna (sadd al-dhara'i'), (2) the action of Umar (ra) and Aisha's confirmation, (3) the hadith about Bani Israel's women.
These are used to specify the general hadiths cited by Shafi'i.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position and its evidence
The text mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i holds it mubah based on the hadiths 'Do not prevent' and 'If she seeks permission, do not prevent her.'
Know these proofs to understand the dispute.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
See how the Hanafi school restricts the general permission using the principle of blocking means to evil (sadd al-dhara'i') and by citing Aisha's statement that the Prophet would have prohibited if he had seen the conditions.
This is a classic case of takhsis (specification) of a general text by other evidence.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on old women
Abu Hanifa restricts old women to Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow all prayers. Understand the reason for the restriction.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school, there is ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ايكره لهن حضور الجماعات، يعنى الشواب منهن لما فيه من خوف الفتنة ترجمہ اور درختوں کے لئے جماعتوں میں حاضر ہونا مکروہ ہے مراد جوان عورتیں ہیں کیونکہ ان کی حاضری میں اتنہ کا خوف ہے۔ تری جوان عورتوں کو جماعتوں میں حاضر ہونا مکروہ ہے۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ عورتوں کا مسجد کی طرف نکلنا مبات ہے امام شافعی کی بیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا تمنعوا آماء الله مساجد اللہ ہے یعنی اللہ کی لونڈیوں کو اللہ کی مساجد سے مت روکو اور ایک روایت میں ہے اذا استاذنت احدكم امرائته الى المسجد فلا يمنعها یعنی جب تم میں سے کسی سے اس کی بیوی مسجد میں جانے کی اجازت مانگے تو منع نہ کرے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جوان عورتوں کی حاضری میں فقہ کا خوف ہے اس لئے ان کو مساجد میں حاضر ہونے سے روکا جائے گا۔ دوسری مال یہ ہے کہ جب حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ نے عورتوں کو مساجد کی طرف نکلنے سے منع کیا تو عورتوں نے حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا سے پکایت کی تو ام المؤمنین نے فرمایا کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو اگر اس حالت کا علم ہو جاتا جس کا عمر کو ہے تو آپا با لکل اجازت نہ اہتے ایک روایت میں ہے کہ ام المومنین نے فرمایا حضور اب جیسی نمازی حالت دیکھتے تو جیسے بنو اسرائیل کی عورتیں ممنوع ہو ئیں تم بھی منع کی جاتیں۔
ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جس کو ابن عبدالبر نے اپنی سند کے ساتھ حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا سے روایت کیا ہے ايها الناس انهوا نساء كم عن لبس الزينته والتبختر فى المساجدفان بني اسرائيل لم يلعنوا حتى لبست نساء هم الزينته وتنجتر و افي المساجد یعنی اے لوگو! اپنی عورتوں کو مسجدوں میں زینت اور تکبر کا لباس پہنے سے منع کرو کیونکہ بنواسرائیل ملعون نہیں ہوئے یہاں تک کہ ان کی عورتوں نے مساجد میں زینت اور فخر و غرور کا لباس پہنا چونکہ ہمارے اس زمانے میں فراق کا غلبہ ہے اس لئے غیر مزین عورتوں کو بھی منع کیا گیا ہے۔
ولاباس للعجوز ان تخرج فى الفجر والمغرب والعشاء وهذا عند ابي حنيفة و قالا يخرجن في الصلوت كلها
It is disapproved for them to attend congregations, meaning young women, due to fear of fitna. [Translation of Urdu: For young women it is makruh to attend congregations. Imam Shafi'i said that women going out to the mosque is mubah (permissible). Shafi'i's proof is the hadith: 'Do not prevent the female servants of Allah from the mosques of Allah' and 'When any of you seeks permission from his wife to go to the mosque, he should not prevent her.' Our proof is that in the presence of young women there is fear of fitna, so they should be prevented from attending. Another proof is that when Umar (ra) prevented women from going out to the mosques, they complained to Aisha (ra), who said: 'If the Prophet (saw) had seen what Umar has seen, he would have prohibited them completely.' Also Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated that Aisha said: 'O people, forbid your women from wearing adornment and walking proudly in the mosques, for the Children of Israel were not cursed until their women did so.' Since in our time corruption prevails, even non-adorned women are prevented. And there is no harm for an old woman to go out for Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha — this is the view of Abu Hanifa, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say she may go out for all prayers.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and a madhhab dispute regarding women's attendance at congregational prayers. The Hanafi ruling: it is makruh (disapproved) for young women (shawab) to attend mosque congregations due to the fear of fitna (temptation). The word 'ikrah' here likely indicates makruh tahrimi given the strong evidence of fitna prevention. Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is mubah (permissible) based on the hadith 'Do not prevent the female servants of Allah from the mosques of Allah.' The Hanafi response uses two proofs: (1) The principle of blocking the means to evil (sadd al-dhara'i') — since fitna is feared, it is better to prevent. (2) The action of Umar (ra) and the confirmation of Aisha (ra) who stated that if the Prophet (saw) were aware of the later conditions, he would have prohibited women completely. (3) A hadith from Ibn Abd al-Barr about the women of Bani Israel who were cursed due to their adornment in mosques. Because in the commentator's time corruption was widespread, even women without adornment are included in the discouragement. The passage then addresses old women (ajuz): according to Abu Hanifa, she may attend Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha prayers only, as these are times when fitna is less likely. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say she may attend all prayers. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is likely the view of Abu Hanifa due to greater caution, but the later practice may follow the Sahibayn if corruption is less.

Key Terms
الشواب (al-shawab): young women who are a source of attraction and potential fitna.
العجوز (al-ajuz): an old woman beyond childbearing age, less likely to cause fitna.
المكروه تحريما (al-makruh tahriman): an act that is prohibited according to strong evidence but not of the same degree as haram; it is sinful to perform.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, which prayers may an old woman attend in the mosque?
A) All five prayers
B) Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha
C) Only Fajr and Maghrib
D) No prayers at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on women attending mosques is nuanced: young women are discouraged due to fitna, while old women may attend with restrictions, reflecting the principle of sadd al-dhara'i'.

Old Women Attending Congregational Prayers: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on old women attending different prayers with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on old women attending congregational prayers and identify the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
Old women may attend only three prayers according to Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn allow all, but later fatwa forbids all due to corruption.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), on whether old women ('ajuz) may attend congregational prayers. The ruling hinges on the potential for fitnah and varies by prayer time. The later Hanafi tradition adapts the ruling due to widespread societal corruption.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify which prayers Abu Hanifa allows and which he prohibits for old women. Note his reasoning: intense desire can cause fitnah, but during Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha the wicked are occupied.
Abu Hanifa allows only these three prayers; Zuhr, Asr, and Jumu'ah are prohibited.
2
State the Sahibayn's position
Identify that the Sahibayn allow old women to attend all congregational prayers. Their reasoning: no desire in old women, so no fitnah, analogous to Eid prayer.
They reject the distinction between prayer times.
3
Follow the proof of each
Examine the evidence: Abu Hanifa cites the intensity of desire (shiddat al-shahwa) causing fitnah. Sahibayn rely on the lack of desire and analogy with Eid. The author of Hidayah rebuts the Eid analogy.
The author argues Eid is in open fields where separation is easy, unlike mosque.
4
Analyse the tarjih (preference)
The author of Hidayah sides with Abu Hanifa, but the later fatwa (from 'Inayah) declares it makruh for all prayers due to general corruption.
This shows how rulings can change with time (taghayyur al-ahkam).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling today: old women should not go out for any congregational prayer because of widespread fitnah.
This is a fatwa from the later scholars (mutakhkhirin).

Translation: And there is no harm for an old woman to go out for Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Translation: The two companions (Sahibayn) said that old women may go out for all prayers because due to lack of desire there is no fitnah, unlike a healthy woman. And in Eid it is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that intense desire leads to intercourse, so fitnah will occur. Except that the wicked ones spread during Zuhr, Asr, and Jumu'ah, while during Fajr and Isha they sleep, and at Maghrib they are busy with food. The wilderness is vast, so women can separate from men. Therefore, going out for Eid is not makruh. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa prohibited old women from going out at Zuhr and Asr but allowed Fajr, Isha, and Maghrib. Sahibayn allowed all. Their proof: old women have little inclination, so no fitnah, like Eid. Regarding Eid, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one via Hasan that they pray in last row; another via Mu'alla from Abu Yusuf that they stand aside without praying, as menstruating women were commanded to attend Eid. Thus, going out for Eid is for gathering not prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: intense desire causes fitnah, so old women also cause fitnah. But the wicked are active during Zuhr, Asr, Jumu'ah, so they should not go out at those times. At Fajr and Isha they sleep, at Maghrib busy eating. Therefore, in those three times there is security, so permission is given. The author of Hidayah says Sahibayn's analogy with Eid is incorrect because Eid prayer is generally in the wilderness where women can stand aside, so it is not makruh. Benefit: Today because of widespread corruption, old women going out for all prayers is makruh. (Inayah)
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on old women (a'juz) attending congregational prayers. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (Sahibayn). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that old women may only go out for Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha prayers, not for Zuhr, Asr, or Jumu'ah. His reasoning is that even old women can incite desire due to intense sexual drive, leading to fitnah. However, during Fajr and Isha people are asleep, at Maghrib busy eating, so the danger is minimal. Sahibayn allow all prayers, arguing that old women have low desire, so no fitnah, analogous to Eid prayer where women go out. The author of Hidayah (Al-Marghinani) rejects the analogy because Eid prayer is in open fields where separation is possible. He concludes with a fatwa that due to widespread corruption today, it is makruh for old women to go out for any congregational prayer. This shows how rulings can adapt to changing societal conditions (taghayyur al-ahkam).

Key Terms
عجوز (ajuz): An old woman beyond the age of desire.
فتنة (fitnah): Social discord or temptation, often sexual in nature.
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two major disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of Al-Hidayah, which of the following is a reason why Sahibayn's analogy with Eid is flawed?
A) Eid prayer is wajib while other prayers are sunnah
B) Eid prayer is performed in open fields where women can stand apart
C) Old women are exempt from Eid prayer
D) Eid prayer is only once a year

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school demonstrates flexibility: Abu Hanifa's position was time-specific, but later scholars expanded the restriction due to societal corruption.

Pure Person Praying Behind a Mustahadah: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof: a pure person cannot pray behind a mustahadah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pure person praying behind a mustahadah and explain the proof based on the hadith 'al-imam damin' and the principle of encompassment.

Core Idea
A pure person cannot pray behind a ma'dhur because the imam's prayer must encompass the follower's, and the weaker cannot encompass the stronger.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author addresses a key issue in congregational prayer: the validity of following an imam whose state of purity is deficient. The ruling is derived from a profound application of the hadith 'al-imam damin', as understood by the Hanafi school. Understanding this ruling illuminates the principle that the imam's prayer must be at least as complete as the follower's.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage clearly states that a pure person (whether man or woman) cannot pray behind a mustahadah (a woman with chronic bleeding) or anyone in a similar state of chronic excuse (ma'dhur). This is a prohibition that renders the prayer invalid.
The ruling is general: it applies to both genders and to any ma'dhur, not just mustahadah.
2
Understand the key principle
The basis is the hadith 'al-imam damin'. The Hanafi school interprets 'damin' to mean that the imam's prayer encompasses (or guarantees) the follower's prayer. A corollary is that 'a thing does not encompass what is above it'—the weaker cannot encompass the stronger.
This interpretation is unique to the Hanafis; other schools may view 'damin' differently.
3
Apply the principle to the case
A pure person's state of purity is stronger (more complete) than that of a ma'dhur (who has a continuous excuse). Since the imam's prayer must encompass the follower's, but a weaker state cannot encompass a stronger one, the imam's prayer cannot cover the follower's. Thus, the prayer is invalid.
The strength lies in the completeness of purity: a pure person's wudu is not deficient, whereas a ma'dhur's wudu is constantly compromised.
4
Recognize the logical basis
The reasoning is based on logical necessity: for the imam's prayer to be valid for the follower, it must be at least equal in effectiveness. If the imam's state is inferior, the follower's prayer is not properly represented, leading to invalidity.
This principle applies to all similar situations where the follower's state is superior to the imam's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يصلي الطاهر خلف من هو فى معنى المستحاضة ولا الطاهرة خلف المستحاضة لان الصحيح اقوى حالا من المعذور والشئى لا يتضمن ماهو فوقه والامام ضامن بمعنى تضمن صلوته صلوة المقتدى
رجمہ اور پاک مرد اس شخص کے پیچھے نماز نہ پڑھے جو مستحاضہ کے حکم میں ہے اور نہ پاک عورت مستحاضہ کے پیچھے نماز پڑھے کیونکہ تندرست کا حال یہ نسبت معذور کے اقوی ہے اور شئے اپنے سے مافوق کو متضمن نہیں ہوتی حالانکہ امام ضامن ہے ابا این معنی کہ امام کی نماز خندی کی نماز کو تضمن ہے۔ فریح مستحاضہ اور جو مستحاضہ کے حکم میں ہے فقہا کی اصطلاح میں اس کو معذور کہتے ہیں پس اب صورت مسئلہ یہ ہوگی کہ پاک مرد مند در مرد کے پیچھے نماز نہ پڑھے اور نہ پاک عورت مستحاضہ عورت کے پیچھے پڑھے۔ دلیل سے پہلے یہ بات ذہن نشین کر لیجئے کہ اس طرح تمام مسائل کی اصل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول الامام ضامن ہے اور حدیث کے معنی نہیں کہ امام کی نماز مقتدی کی نماز کو تضمن ہے یہ معنی نہیں کہ امام مقتدی کی نماز کا ذمہ دار یعنی مکلف ہے دوسری بات کہ شے اپنے سے کمتر کو ضمن ہوتی ہے یا اپنے ہم مثل کو لیکن اپنے سے مافوق کو متضمن نہیں ہوتی ۔
اب دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں مقتدی چونکہ پاک اور غیر معذور ہے اور امام معذور کے حکم میں ہے اس لئے مقتدی کی نماز کا حال امام کی نماز سے اقوی اور ارفع ہے اور امام کی نماز کا حال کمتر اور ادنی ہے اور چونکہ کمتر اور اضعف اقوی کو متضمن نہیں ہوتا اس لئے امام کی نماز مقتدی کی نماز کو تضمن نہیں ہوگی حالانکہ امام کی نماز مقتدی کی نماز کو متضمن ہوتی ہے اس لئے پاک اور غیر معذور مرد کا مندور کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس طرح پاک عورت کی نماز مستحاضہ کے پیچھے درست نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ مستحاضہ کی نماز کا حال مقتدی عورت کی نماز کے حال سے ناقص
He said: A pure man should not pray behind one who is in the state of a mustahadah, nor a pure woman behind a mustahadah, because the healthy person's state is stronger than the excused person's, and a thing does not encompass what is above it. The imam is a guarantor, meaning his prayer encompasses the prayer of the follower. Translation: A pure man should not pray behind someone who is in the rule of a mustahadah, nor a pure woman behind a mustahadah, because a healthy person's state is stronger relative to an excused person, and a thing does not encompass what is above it. The imam is a guarantor, meaning the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's prayer. Mustahadah and one in its rule are called ma'dhur in juristic terminology. So the ruling is that a pure healthy man should not pray behind a ma'dhur man, nor a pure woman behind a mustahadah woman. Before the proof, understand that the basis of all such issues is the Prophet's saying: 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor). The meaning is not that the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's; rather, the imam is responsible for the follower's prayer. Second, a thing encompasses what is below it or equal to it, but not what is above it. The gist of the proof is that in the mentioned case, the follower is pure and not excused, while the imam is in the state of an excused person, so the follower's prayer state is stronger and higher, and the imam's state is weaker and lower. Since the weaker does not encompass the stronger, the imam's prayer will not encompass the follower's prayer. The imam's prayer must encompass the follower's, therefore it is not permissible for a pure healthy man to follow a ma'dhur. Similarly, a pure woman's prayer behind a mustahadah is not valid because the mustahadah's prayer state is deficient compared to the follower's.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a person who is pure (having wudu or ghusl) cannot pray behind an imam who is in a state of chronic ritual impurity, such as a mustahadah (a woman with chronic bleeding) or a ma'dhur (someone with a continuous excuse like incontinence). The proof is based on the hadith 'al-imam damin', which the Hanafis interpret as meaning the imam's prayer encompasses (or guarantees) the follower's prayer. A key principle is that something can only encompass something equal or lesser, not greater. Since the pure person's prayer is more complete (stronger) than the ma'dhur's, the imam's weaker prayer cannot encompass the follower's stronger one, so the prayer is invalid. This reasoning is used to derive many similar rulings. The commentary explains the logical basis: the imam's prayer must be at least as perfect as the follower's; if the imam is deficient (due to his excuse), the follower's prayer is not fully represented.

Key Terms
مستحاضة (mustahadah): A woman with chronic bleeding who must perform wudu for each prayer and can pray despite bleeding.
معذور (ma'dhur): A person with a continuous excuse like incontinence, whose state of purity is deficient.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; in this context, the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the mustahadah is not a valid imam for anyone
B) Because the mustahadah's prayer is weaker and cannot encompass the stronger prayer of the pure person
C) Because it is disliked (makruh) but valid
D) Because the hadith forbids it explicitly

Key Takeaway
The imam's prayer must encompass the follower's; thus a pure person cannot pray behind a ma'dhur.

Prohibited Imam-Follower Pairings in Prayer
Ruling statement: prohibitions in imam-follower pairing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two prohibited imam-follower pairings and explain the underlying principle that the imam must be equal or superior in recitation and covering.

Core Idea
An imam must be at least as proficient and covered as his follower.

The Hanafi school establishes clear rules for who may lead whom in congregational prayer. This lesson presents two specific prohibitions: a qari (someone who recites Quran well) cannot pray behind an ummi (someone who cannot recite properly), and a properly clothed person cannot pray behind a naked person. These rulings stem from the fundamental principle that the imam's state must be equal or superior to that of the follower in the essential conditions of prayer. The text is a concise ruling statement commonly found in classical Hanafi manuals, emphasising the necessity of maintaining the honour and validity of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited scenarios
Read the Arabic text carefully. Note the two prohibitions: (1) a qari behind an ummi, (2) a clothed person behind a naked person. Understand that both prohibitions are explicitly stated using the negation 'لا' (not).
2
Extract the underlying principle
The text gives the reason as 'li-quwwati hālihā' (because their state is stronger). This indicates that the imam must have a state (condition) at least as strong as the follower. The principle is that the imam must be equal or superior in the essential aspects of prayer, here recitation ability and covering of 'awrah.
This principle is also found in other rulings, e.g., a fasiq cannot lead a righteous person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصلـى القارى خلف الأمى ولا المكتسى خلف العارى لِقُوَّةِ حالها
ترجمہ اور قاری امی کے پیچھے نہ پڑھے اور نہ کپڑ اپنے والا ننگے کے پیچھے پڑھے کیونکہ قاری اور مکتسی کا حال بہ نسبت امی اور ننگے کے قومی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ اور اس کی دلیل واضح ہے۔
And the qari should not pray behind the ummi, nor the clothed person behind the naked, because their state is stronger. Translation: The qari should not pray behind an ummi, nor a clothed person behind a naked one, because the qari and clothed person's state is stronger compared to the ummi and naked. Explanation: The ruling and its proof are clear.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement. A qari (someone who recites Quran well) cannot follow an ummi (someone who cannot recite properly) in prayer because qira'ah is a pillar; the imam must be at least as proficient as the follower. Similarly, a clothed person cannot follow a naked person because covering the awrah is a condition; the imam must be at least as covered. The reasoning is the same as the previous lesson: the imam's state must be equal or superior to the follower's. The commentator says the proof is clear from the principle of 'al-imam damin'.

Key Terms
قارئ (qari): A person who recites the Quran correctly and can recite properly in prayer.
أمي (ummi): An illiterate person who cannot recite Quran correctly.
مكتسي (muktasī): A clothed person (wearing sufficient covering).
عار (ārī): A naked person (without covering).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson's ruling, which of the following is prohibited?
A) A qari praying behind another qari
B) A clothed person praying behind a naked person
C) An ummi praying behind a qari
D) A naked person praying alone

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the imam must be equal or superior to the follower in recitation and covering; violating this is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).

Ruling on Tayammum Imam Leading Those with Wudu
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum imam leading wudu holders.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a mutayammim leading those with wudu and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
A mutayammim can lead those with wudu according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad objects.

This passage presents a concise intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of a person who has performed tayammum (dry purification) leading in prayer those who have wudu. The ruling touches on the status of tayammum as a valid purification. Let's examine the positions and their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and the act
Determine who is being discussed (mutayammim and mutawaddi'un) and what act is being ruled upon (imamah/leading prayer).
2
State the Hanafi position
Identify the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: it is permissible. Then note the dissenting view of Muhammad.
3
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
Understand the argument: Muhammad says it is not permissible because tayammum is a lesser purification. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf deem it sufficient for leading prayer.
The underlying principle: tayammum is valid purification for prayer, thus the imam's state is adequate.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify the relied-upon position for fatwa: permissibility (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah favors this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز ان يؤم المتيمـم المـتوضيين وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد لايجوز لانه طهارة.
It is permissible for a person with tayammum to lead those with wudu. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said it is not permissible because (tayammum) is a (lower) purification.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This is a short intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling: It is permissible for a person who performed tayammum (due to unavailability of water) to lead in prayer those who have wudu. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, saying it is not permissible because tayammum is a lesser form of purification (it is only a substitute and has limitations). The reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that tayammum is a valid purification that lifts the state of hadath in the absence of water, so the imam is considered pure enough to lead even those with wudu. Imam Muhammad's view is based on the principle that the imam's state should not be deficient; tayammum is less permanent than wudu. However, the relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as mentioned in the Hidayah and other works.

Key Terms
متيمم (mutayammim): A person who has performed tayammum instead of wudu or ghusl.
متوضئ (mutawaddi'): A person with wudu (water purification).
طهارة (taharah): Purification; in this context, tayammum is a form of taharah but considered lesser by Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if the followers also have tayammum

Key Takeaway
A mutayammim may lead those with wudu according to the majority Hanafi view; the dissenting view of Muhammad is not the mufta bihi.

Ruling on a Pure Person Praying Behind a Mustahadah
State the prohibition and provide proof from hadith and legal reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pure person praying behind a mustahadah and explain the proof from the hadith 'al-imam damin' and the principle of inclusion.

Core Idea
A weaker state cannot encompass a stronger, so a pure person cannot pray behind a mustahadah.

The Hanafi school rules that a person in a state of complete purity (tahir) cannot validly pray behind someone who is excused (ma'dhur), such as a mustahadah. This ruling is derived from the prophetic saying 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor) and the logical principle that a weaker ritual state cannot encompass a stronger one. In this lesson, you will learn the ruling, its proof, and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the explicit ruling: a pure person (male or female) cannot pray behind a mustahadah or any ma'dhur. The prayer is invalid (batil) if performed.
2
Understand Key Terms
Define 'mustahadah' (woman with chronic bleeding), 'ma'dhur' (excused person), and the hadith 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor). Recognize that the hadith implies the imam's prayer includes the follower's.
The hadith is interpreted by Hanafis to mean inclusion, not just responsibility.
3
Analyze the Proof
Walk through the reasoning: The imam's prayer must include the follower's. But a weaker state (ma'dhur) cannot encompass a stronger state (tahir). Therefore, the imam's prayer cannot include the follower's, making the prayer invalid.
This principle applies to all cases where the follower's ritual purity is superior.
4
Apply the Principle
Consider analogous cases: a person with full wudu cannot follow someone with tayammum; a person without a chronic excuse cannot follow a ma'dhur. The key is the relative strength of ritual states.

So the conclusion: a mustahadah and one who is in the ruling of a mustahadah is called a ma'dhur in the terminology of the jurists. So now the case is that a pure man should not pray behind the mentioned man, nor a pure woman behind a mustahadah woman. Before the proof, note that the basis of all such issues is the saying of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم 'al-imam damin', and the meaning of the hadith is that the imam's prayer includes the follower's prayer; it means that the imam is responsible for the follower's prayer, i.e., obliged. Second, a thing includes what is lesser than itself or its equal, but it does not include what is above itself. Now the summary of the proof is that in the mentioned case, the follower is pure and not excused, and the imam is in the ruling of excused, so the state of the follower's prayer is stronger and higher than the imam's prayer, and the imam's prayer is lower and weaker. Since the weaker and lower does not include the stronger, the imam's prayer will not include the follower's prayer, whereas the imam's prayer should include the follower's prayer. Therefore, a pure and non-excused man following an excused one is not permissible. Similarly, a pure woman's prayer behind a mustahadah is not valid because the state of the mustahadah's prayer is deficient compared to the female follower's prayer.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that a pure person (tahir) cannot pray behind a person who is legally excused (ma'dhur), such as a mustahadah or someone in a similar continuous state of ritual impurity. The proof is based on the hadith 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor), which means the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's prayer. The underlying principle is that a weaker state cannot encompass a stronger one. Since the follower's purity is stronger than the imam's excused state, the imam's prayer cannot include the follower's, making this form of prayer invalid. The text explains that the follower must be equal or lesser in ritual status for the imam's prayer to be valid. Thus, a person with complete wudu cannot follow one with tayammum, etc.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustahāḍah): A woman with chronic non-menstrual bleeding; in this context, a type of ma'dhur whose wudu is invalidated by continuous bleeding.
المعذور (al-ma‘dhūr): A person with a valid excuse, such as continuous bleeding or incontinence, whose ithar is excused but their state is considered weaker than a pure person.
الامام ضامن (al-imāmu ḍāmin): A prophetic saying meaning the imam is a guarantor; interpreted as the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's prayer.

Dispute on Mutayammim Leading Those with Wudu
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Shaykhayn allow, Muhammad disallows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on a mutayammim leading those with wudu and explain the reasoning of each position.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, a mutayammim can lead those with wudu—the Shaykhayn equate tayammum with wudu as absolute purification.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: can a person who has performed tayammum lead in prayer those who have wudu? Imam Muhammad argues that tayammum is a secondary purification, so the follower's wudu state is stronger and cannot be led by a weaker imam. However, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) hold that tayammum is an absolute purification, equal in status to wudu, making such leadership permissible. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi scholars classify purification types and apply qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit a mutayammim to lead those with wudu, while Imam Muhammad disallows it.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab dispute.
2
Follow Imam Muhammad's proof
Examine Muhammad's argument: tayammum is necessary purification (ṭahārah ḍarūriyyah) while wudu is original (aṣliyyah); the weaker cannot lead the stronger.
Muhammad uses qiyas based on the principle of strength of purification.
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's proof
The Shaykhayn respond that tayammum is absolute purification (ṭahārah muṭlaqah), not time-bound, and therefore its state equals wudu.
They argue that because tayammum remains valid indefinitely as long as the excuse exists, it is not inferior.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the Shaykhayn, if a mutayammim leads, the followers' prayer is valid; according to Muhammad, it is invalid.
This affects the validity of congregational prayer in communities where the imam has a chronic water excuse.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Shaykhayn: it is permissible. This is the dominant view in the Hanafi school.
Later Hanafi authorities prefer the Shaykhayn's view due to its stronger proof.

And it is permissible for a mutayammim to lead those who have wudu – this according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said it is not permissible because tayammum is a necessary purification and purification with water is original. For the two (Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf): it is an absolute purification, and therefore it is not limited to a measure ... Translation: And it is permissible for a mutayammim to lead those with wudu, and this is according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad said it is not permissible because tayammum is a necessary purification and purification with water is original. The proof of the Shaykhayn is that tayammum is absolute purification because it is not limited to the extent of need. Explanation: There is disagreement about whether a mutayammim can lead those with wudu. The Shaykhayn permit it, and Imam Muhammad holds that he cannot. Imam Muhammad's proof: tayammum is necessary purification and purification with water is original; there is no doubt that the one with original purification has a stronger state than the one with necessary purification. Thus the follower is stronger and the imam weaker, and it is established that a weaker person cannot lead a stronger one. Therefore we say: it is not permissible for a mutayammim to lead those with wudu. The proof of the Shaykhayn: tayammum is absolute purification, not time-limited, like the purification of a mustahadah, because the effective cause is that tayammum is not limited to the extent of need; rather, even if water is unavailable for ten years, tayammum remains valid. So when tayammum is absolute purification, the state of the mutayammim and the one with wudu is equal, and when they are equal, one can lead the other.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a person who performs tayammum can lead those who have wudu in prayer. Imam Muhammad argues it is not permissible because tayammum is a secondary, necessary form of purification, while wudu is primary and stronger. Since the follower (with wudu) has a stronger state, the imam (with tayammum) cannot lead him, based on the principle that the weaker cannot contain the stronger. In contrast, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) argue that tayammum is an absolute form of purification, not restricted to a specific time or need. Since it is valid for any prayer as long as the excuse exists, its state is equal to that of wudu. Therefore, a mutayammim can lead those with wudu. The text also references a narration (روى ان الـ) that is incomplete in the OCR. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to later Hanafi authorities is the view of the Shaykhayn, i.e., it is permissible.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry purification with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
طهارة ضرورية (ṭahārah ḍarūriyyah): Purification that is necessary due to excuse, considered secondary to original purification.
طهارة أصلية (ṭahārah aṣliyyah): Original purification with water, which is the primary and default method.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a mutayammim can lead those with wudu because tayammum is considered absolute purification equal in status to wudu.

Ruling on a Masih Leading Those Who Wash Feet
Ruling with proof for permissibility of masih leading ghasil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a masih leading those who wash their feet, explain the qiyas jaliy proof, and distinguish it from the mustahadah case.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuff equals washing feet in removing hadath, so a masih can lead those who wash.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical imamah question: can a person who wiped over leather socks (khuff) lead a congregation whose members washed their feet? The Hanafi ruling is yes, based on qiyas jaliy: wiping removes the hadath just as washing does. A key contrast is drawn with the mustahadah, who cannot lead because her hadath is deemed not fully removed by Shariah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
The ruling is about imamah: the permissibility of a person who wipes over khuff (masih) leading those who wash their feet (ghasilin). The Hanafi position is that it is permissible (mubah).
The ruling applies specifically to prayer (salah).
2
Understand the qiyas proof
The proof is qiyas jaliy: the asl (original case) is washing feet, which removes hadath. The far‘ (new case) is wiping over khuff. The illa (effective cause) is the removal of hadath from the foot, whether by direct washing or by wiping over the barrier (khuff) which prevents hadath from reaching the foot. Since wiping removes the hadath that settled on the khuff, the state of purity is complete, similar to washing.
The analogy holds because both achieve purification of the feet for prayer.
3
Note the contrast with mustahadah
The text contrasts the masih with a mustahadah (a woman with chronic vaginal bleeding). For the mustahadah, her hadath is continuous and Shariah does not consider it removed, even though she performs wudu for each prayer. Thus, her purification is deficient, preventing her from leading those who are fully pure. This contrast reinforces the completeness of the mas'h purification.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the strength of the qiyas.
4
Consider cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Imām al-Shafi‘ī) may view wiping as a temporary concession and consider the purification less complete. The Hanafi response, as reflected in this text, is that the hadath is effectively removed by wiping, so the masih is in an equivalent state to the ghasil. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤم الماسح الغاسلين لان الخف مانع سراية الحدث الى القدم وماحل بالخف يزيله المسح بخلاف المستحاضة لان الحدث لم يعتبر زواله شرعا مع قيامه حق

Explanation: The case is that one who wipes over khuff can lead those who wash their feet. As for the hadath that settled on the khuff, wiping removes it, so the person with khuff is like one who washed his feet.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof supporting the validity of a person who wipes over leather socks (khuff) leading in prayer those who wash their feet. The proof is that the khuff prevents the hadath from reaching the foot, and wiping (mas'h) removes the hadath that has occurred to the khuff, making the state equivalent to washing. The text contrasts this with the mustahadah, whose hadath is continuous and not considered removed by Shariah, making her state weaker. Thus, the masih is in an equal state to the ghasil, so he can lead them.

Key Terms

الغاسل (al-ghāsil): The person who washes his feet directly in wudu.
الخف (al-khuff): Leather socks that can be wiped over during wudu.

The Tayammum Imam: Can the Dry Purified Lead the Water Purified?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum imam leading wudu performers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on the tayammum imam leading wudu performers and explain the reasoning of each side.

Core Idea
Tayammum, when valid, is absolute purification equal to wudu, so the tayammum imam may lead — but Imam Muhammad disagrees.

This lesson explores an important intra-Hanafi disagreement: may a person who performed tayammum lead in prayer those who performed wudu? The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say yes, while Imam Muhammad says no. The difference hinges on whether tayammum is considered absolute purification (taharah mutlaqah) or merely necessary purification (taharah daruriyyah). Let's examine the proofs of each side.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core question: Can a person with tayammum legitimately act as imam for persons with wudu?
The ruling affects the validity of the congregation's prayer.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: permissible. Imam Muhammad: not permissible.
These are both within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's dalil
He uses qiyas: wudu is original purification (taharah asliyyah), tayammum is necessary (taharah daruriyyah). A person with a lesser state cannot lead one with a greater state.
Imam Muhammad considers the imam's state inferior.
4
Analyze the two shaykhs' dalil
They counter that tayammum is absolute purification (taharah mutlaqah) because it is not temporally limited; as long as the excuse persists, it remains valid for years, just like wudu. Thus the states are equal.
They rely on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practically, if a tayammum imam leads wudu performers, the two shaykhs deem the prayer valid; Imam Muhammad deems it invalid. The text implies the two shaykhs' view is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
The difference affects whether followers must repeat their prayer.

Chapter of Imamate. 111- Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Ashraf al-Hidaya: [Tayammum is] necessary and purification with water is original. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that it (tayammum) is absolute purification, therefore it is not limited to a specific amount. Explanation: The translation: For the one performing tayammum, leading those with wudu is permissible, and this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad says it is not permissible because tayammum is necessary purification and purification with water is original. And the proof of the two shaykhs is that tayammum is absolute purification, since due to excuse it is not limited to the amount of need. Explanation: There is disagreement whether one with tayammum can follow one with wudu. The two shaykhs declared it permissible, and Imam Muhammad holds that it is not. It is narrated that... Explanation: Imam Muhammad's proof is that tayammum is necessary purification and purification with water is original purification, and there is no doubt that the one who has original purification has a stronger state compared to the one who has necessary purification. So it is known that the follower is strong and stronger than the state of the imam. And it is accepted that a person of a lesser state cannot follow one of a greater state. Therefore we say that for the one with tayammum, leading those with wudu is not permissible. The proof of the two shaykhs is that tayammum is absolute purification, not limited in time, i.e., tayammum is purification absolutely, like the purification of a mustahadah, not limited, because the existing reason is that tayammum is not limited to the amount of need, rather even for ten years if water is not available or one cannot use it because of illness, tayammum will remain legislated. So when tayammum is absolute purification, both the one with tayammum and the one with wudu have equal states. And when their states are equal, one can lead the other.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a person who performs tayammum can lead in prayer those who performed wudu. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permit it, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it. Imam Muhammad's argument relies on qiyas: wudu is original purification (taharah asliyyah) and thus stronger than tayammum which is merely necessary purification (taharah daruriyyah). A person with a lesser state (the tayammum performer) cannot lead one with a greater state (the wudu performer). The two shaykhs counter that tayammum is absolute purification (taharah mutlaqah) in the sense that it is not temporally limited; as long as the excuse exists, tayammum remains valid even for years, similar to the purification of a mustahadah. Thus both tayammum and wudu are equal in being valid purification, and the imam's state is not inferior. The text then explains that the two shaykhs' view is based on istihsan, considering the continuous validity of tayammum. The passage does not explicitly state who wins, but the structure suggests the view of the two shaykhs is preferred as it is introduced as the jayiz position.

Key Terms
تیمم (tayammum): Dry purification using earth or similar when water is unavailable or harmful.
طہارت مطلقہ (taharah mutlaqah): Absolute purification; a purification that is not limited in time or scope, like wudu and ghusl.
امامت (imamah): Leading the congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The key difference is whether tayammum is considered absolute purification equal to wudu (two shaykhs) or merely a necessary purification inferior to wudu (Imam Muhammad).

Imam with Masah Leading Foot-Washers
Ruling and proof on imam with masah leading foot-washers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a person who wiped over khuffs can lead those who washed their feet, and apply the qiyas between khuff and mustahadah.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs makes one legally equivalent to one who washed feet for imamah.

This passage addresses a specific question of leadership in prayer: can a person who performed wudu by wiping over khuffs lead others who washed their feet? The Hanafi school answers yes, based on a clear analogy (qiyas). The reasoning involves the concept of hadath being confined and removed by wiping.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage states that a person who wiped over khuffs may lead those who washed their feet in prayer. This is a ruling of permissibility (mubah).
No obligation or prohibition is implied.
2
Identify the Proof
The khuff prevents hadath from reaching the foot. When a person had washed his feet, put on khuffs, and then experienced hadath, the hadath is confined to the khuff. Wiping removes that hadath, restoring purity equivalent to having washed the feet.
The proof is based on the function of the khuff as a barrier and the effectiveness of masah.
3
Contrast with Mustahadah
The text contrasts with a mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding). In her case, hadath is not considered removed by Shariah even after wudu, because the bleeding continues. She is therefore not equivalent to a pure person.
This contrast highlights that khuff-wiper is superior in purity to mustahadah for leading prayer.
4
Extract the Qiyas
The ruling is derived via qiyas: the foot-washer (asl) is pure and may lead; the khuff-wiper (far) has equivalent purity because the khuff prevents hadath from reaching the foot and masah removes it. The common illa is effective removal of hadath from the foot.
The mustahadah is excluded because her hadath is not removed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤم الماسح الغاسلين لان الخف مانع سراية الحدث الى القدم وماحل بالخف يزيله المسح بخلاف المستحاضة لان الحدث لم يعتبر زواله شرعا مع قيامه حق

And the one who wipes (over khuffs) can lead those who wash (their feet), because the khuff prevents the transmission of hadath to the foot, and what has entered the khuff is removed by wiping, unlike the mustahadah, because the hadath is not considered removed by Shariah while it actually exists. Translation: And the one who wipes can lead those who wash, because the khuff prevents hadath from reaching the foot, and what has entered the khuff is removed by wiping. In contrast to the mustahadah, because hadath is such that its removal is not considered by Shariah, but in reality it exists. Explanation: The case is that the one who wipes over khuffs can lead those who wash feet; the proof is that the owner of the khuff washed his feet then put on the khuffs, and the khuff prevents hadath from reaching the foot, so this person remains like one who washed his feet. The hadath entered the khuff, and the answer is that whatever entered the khuff is removed by wiping, so the person with khuffs remains like one who washed.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling that a person who has wiped over his leather socks (khuffs) during ablution can lead in prayer those who have washed their feet (i.e., without khuffs). The proof is that the khuff prevents the hadath from reaching the foot. When a person performed wudu and then put on khuffs, any subsequent hadath occurs only in the khuff, not on the foot, and wiping the khuff removes that hadath. Thus, the person who wipes is effectively in the same state as one who washed his feet. The text contrasts this with a mustahadah (a woman with chronic bleeding): in her case, the hadath is considered legally present despite continuous flow, so her condition is inferior. The commentary explains that the khuff-wearer is like a foot-washer because the khuff confines the hadath, and wiping removes it.

Key Terms
مسح على الخفين (masah ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks during ablution instead of washing feet, permissible under conditions.
مستحاضة (mustahadah): A woman suffering from chronic uterine bleeding (istihadah), where the flow is continuous but not considered menstrual blood for certain rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage
