Gesture-Performer Leading Another: Ruling and Exception
Ruling on gesture-performer leading another with exception based on position hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a mu'mi leading another mu'mi and identify the exception based on the hierarchy of physical states.

Core Idea
A mu'mi may lead another mu'mi only if states are equal or imam's state is stronger.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario where two individuals are unable to perform the physical movements of prayer and must rely on gestures. The Hanafi school permits a mu'mi to lead another mu'mi if they share the same physical state. However, a critical exception arises when the follower's state is superior to the imam's, based on the strength hierarchy of positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage rules on the permissibility of a mu'mi (gesture-performer) leading another mu'mi. The general ruling is that it is permissible.
The hukm is mubah (permissible).
2
Understand the basis: equality of state
The reason given is 'استوائهما في الحال' (equality of state). This means both are in a similar disability condition, such as both sitting or both lying.
Equality is key; if states differ, the ruling changes.
3
Identify the exception
The text says 'الا ان يومى المؤتم قاعد او الامام مضطجعا' (except if the follower gestures while sitting and the imam is lying). This is the only prohibited combination.
The exception is when the follower's state (sitting) is stronger than the imam's (lying).
4
Understand the rationale
The reason is 'لان القعود معتبر فيثبت به القوة' (because sitting is considered and thus establishes strength). Sitting is a stronger state than lying; one with a stronger state cannot follow one with a weaker state.
This establishes a hierarchy: standing > sitting > lying.
5
Derive the hierarchy
From the exception, we derive that the imam must be at least as strong as the follower. A weaker imam leading a stronger follower is invalid.
Apply this principle to other combinations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلى المؤمى خلف مثله لاستوائهما في الحال الا ان يومى المؤتم قاعد او الامام مضطجعا لان القعود معتبر فيثبت به القوة
And the one who gestures (mu'mi) can pray behind one like him because they are equal in state, unless the follower gestures while sitting and the imam is lying on his side, because sitting is considered (more active) and thus gives strength.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that a person who is forced to pray by gestures (due to extreme illness or disability) can lead another person who also prays by gestures. The reason is that they are equal in their state of inability. However, there is an exception: if the follower is gesturing while sitting and the imam is lying on his side, the follower is not allowed. This is because the sitting position is considered a stronger state than lying on the side, and one with a stronger state cannot follow one with a weaker state. 'Sitting' here indicates a relatively stronger ability compared to reclining.

Key Terms
مؤمي (mu'mi): A person who performs the actions of prayer (like bowing and prostration) by gestures (ishaarah) due to severe illness or inability.
قاعد (qa'id): Sitting position in prayer, considered a stronger state than lying down.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the follower is sitting and the imam is lying
B) When both are standing
C) When the imam is sitting and the follower is standing
D) When both are reclining

Key Takeaway
A mu'mi may lead another mu'mi only if their physical states are equal or the imam's state is stronger; the exception prohibits a sitting follower from following a lying imam.

Standing Person Praying Behind Sitting Imam
Ruling with proof on standing person following sitting imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a standing person following a sitting imam and explain how the prophetic hadith overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
The Prophet’s action overrides analogy: a standing person may follow a sitting imam.

This passage addresses a classical Hanafi dispute: whether a person who can stand can pray behind an imam who sits due to illness. Imam Muhammad argued by qiyas it is impermissible, but Abu Hanifa relied on the explicit hadith of the Prophet’s final prayer. The lesson demonstrates how textual evidence (nas) takes precedence over analogical reasoning (qiyas) in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a standing person (qa'im) following a sitting imam (qa'id) in congregational prayer. The ruling according to the matn is that it is permissible.
The matn states 'وَيُصَلِّى الْقَائِمُ خَلْفَ الْقَاعِدِ' (And the standing person prays behind the sitting person).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of the Prophet's last prayer where he prayed sitting while the congregation stood. The text cites the narration explicitly.
The hadith is famous and recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (fi'l) and his tacit approval (taqrir) by not ordering the congregation to sit indicate the ruling of permissibility. Even though the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), its meaning (dalala) is clear and definitive.
The Arabic phrase used is 'صلى اخر صلاته قاعدا والقوم خلفه قيام' (He prayed his last prayer sitting and the people behind him were standing).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani opposes the ruling based on qiyas: the standing person's state (hal) is stronger (aqwa) than the sitting person's, so he should not follow a weaker imam, analogous to a healthy person not following a sick person who gestures (ima').
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; Abu Yusuf agreed with Abu Hanifa.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school abandons the qiyas because the nas is stronger. The principle is that a zanni nas overrides qiyas. The mufta bihi is permissibility, and the text explicitly says 'وَنَحْنُ تَرَكْنَاهُ بِالنَّصِّ' (we abandon it due to the text).
The tarjih authority is the text itself; no need for external tarjih.

نماز پڑھی اور ابو بکر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نماز کے ساتھ نماز پڑھتے اور لوگ ابوبکر کی نماز کے ساتھ نماز پڑھتے ۔ مراد یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت تانے بیٹھ کر امامت فرمائی اور ابوبکر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی لئے بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنے والے کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے۔
And the standing person prays behind the sitting person, and Muhammad said it is not permissible, and that is the analogy due to the strength of the standing person's state, but we abandon the analogy due to the textual evidence, which is what is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, prayed his last prayer sitting and the people behind him were standing. Translation: The standing person can pray behind the sitting person, and Imam Muhammad said it is not permissible, and that is the analogy because the state of the standing person is stronger, and we abandoned the analogy due to the text, and the text is a hadith narrated that the Prophet performed his last prayer sitting and the people behind him were standing. Explanation: The issue is that the standing person can follow the sitting person. Imam Muhammad said the standing person following the sitting person is not permissible. This is the requirement of analogy because the standing person's state is stronger than the sitting person's state. Just as it is not permissible for a healthy person to follow a sick person who prays with gestures because the healthy person's state is stronger than that sick person, similarly it would not be permissible for the standing person to follow the sitting person. But we abandoned this analogy because of the text. By 'text' is meant this hadith: When the Prophet was in the illness of death, he said to tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer. Hearing this, Aisha said to Hafsah to tell the Messenger of Allah that Abu Bakr is a soft-hearted man; when he stands in your place on the prayer mat, he will not be able to control himself, so command someone else. Aisha said this twice, then the Prophet said, 'You are like the companions of Yusuf, tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer.' When Abu Bakr started the prayer, the Prophet felt relief from his illness, then leaning on Abbas and Ali, he came to the mosque. When Abu Bakr sensed the arrival of the Prophet, he moved back, and the Prophet went forward and prayed sitting, and Abu Bakr prayed with the Prophet's prayer, and the people prayed with Abu Bakr's prayer. The meaning is that the Prophet led sitting, and Abu Bakr said the takbir upon hearing the Prophet's takbir, and the people said takbir upon hearing Abu Bakr's takbir. This is the last prayer in which the Prophet led. From this hadith it is understood that it is permissible for those praying standing to follow one who is praying sitting.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the permissibility of a standing person following a sitting imam. The matn states that a standing person may pray behind a sitting imam. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds it impermissible based on qiyas (analogy): the standing person's state (hal) is stronger (aqwa) than the sitting person's, just as a healthy person may not follow a sick person who gestures in prayer. Despite this strong qiyas, the Hanafi school adopts the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, allowing it, because a specific text (nas) from the Sunnah overrides the analogy. The text is the well-known hadith of the Prophet's final illness where he prayed sitting while the people behind him stood. The commentary narrates the full incident, explaining that the Prophet led the prayer sitting, Abu Bakr conveyed the takbir, and the congregation followed. This provides clear scriptural authority for the ruling. The passage also illustrates the Hanafi principle that a zanni dalil (qiyas) is abandoned in the face of a stronger nas.

Key Terms
قائم (qa'im): A person standing in prayer, able to perform ruku' and sujood normally.
قاعد (qa'id): A person sitting in prayer due to inability to stand, but still able to bow and prostrate normally.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings when no explicit text is found.
نص (nas): Explicit textual evidence from the Quran or Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is impermissible because the imam's state is weaker.
B) It is permissible based on the Prophet's action in his final illness.
C) It is permissible only if the follower also sits.
D) It is impermissible unless the imam is sick.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a standing person may pray behind a sitting imam because the prophetic nas overrides the qiyas.

Person Gesturing Behind Gesturing Imam
Ruling on mu'mi following mu'mi with exception for stronger follower state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mu'mi following a mu'mi and identify the exceptional case where it is impermissible.

Core Idea
A gesturing follower cannot follow a gesturing imam if the follower's state is stronger.

In the Hanafi school, the validity of following an imam in prayer depends on equality of states. This passage addresses individuals who pray with gestures due to incapacity, clarifying when following is permissible and when it is not. The key principle is that the follower's state may not be stronger than the imam's.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The passage states that a mu'mi (one who prays with gestures) may follow another mu'mi. This is permissible (jawaz) because their states are equal in incapacity.
This applies when both are in a state of inability to perform ruku' and sujood.
2
Recognize the exception
Following is not permissible when the follower gestures while sitting and the imam gestures while lying down. The follower's state is stronger (sitting) than the imam's (lying).
The imam's state is weaker, and the stronger cannot follow the weaker.
3
Understand the reasoning
Sitting is considered a valid pillar in prayer with gestures, giving it legal strength (quwwah). In contrast, standing while gesturing is not a pillar and is better omitted, so it does not confer strength.
Thus, a sitting follower has a stronger state than a lying imam, making iqtida' invalid.
4
Distinguish the permissible scenario
If the imam sits and the follower stands (both gesturing), following is permissible because standing in this case is not a pillar, so states are effectively equal.
The standing follower's state is not considered stronger because standing is not a pillar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the gesturing person prays behind one like him, due to equality of state, except if the follower gestures sitting and the imam lies down, because sitting is considered and with it strength is established. Translation: The gesturing person can pray behind his like, because they are equal in state, except if the follower gestures sitting and the imam lies down, because sitting is considered and thus strength is established. Explanation: The issue is that a person who prays with gestures can follow another person who also prays with gestures, even if the imam gestures sitting and the follower gestures standing. Because when standing and gesturing, standing is not a pillar, rather it is better to omit it, so this standing is in the ruling of non-standing. The conclusion is that imam and follower are equal in state, so following is permissible. However, if the follower gestures sitting and the imam gestures lying down, then following is not permissible because sitting is a valid pillar. The evidence is that if one is able to gesture sitting, it is not permissible to perform nafl prayer lying down. So it is known that sitting is a valid pillar, and with it strength is established for the follower which is not present for the imam. This is because the stronger state may not follow the weaker state; therefore the one sitting and gesturing may not follow the one lying and gesturing.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about a person who prays with gestures (mu'mi) following another such person. The principle is that if both are equal in their state of inability, following is permissible. For example, an imam who gestures while sitting can be followed by a follower who gestures while standing, because the standing in this case is not a pillar. However, if the follower gestures while sitting (a stronger state) and the imam gestures while lying down (weaker), following is impermissible because sitting has legal strength (quwwah). The commentary clarifies that sitting is a valid pillar in such cases, distinguishing it from standing when gesturing.

Key Terms
مؤمى (mu'mi): A person who prays with gestures (ishaarah) due to inability to perform ruku' and sujood normally.
اقتداء (iqtida'): The act of following an imam in congregational prayer.
حال (hal): The physical state or condition of the person in prayer, e.g., standing, sitting, lying, or gesturing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When both gesture from a sitting position.
B) When the imam gestures sitting and the follower gestures lying down.
C) When the follower gestures sitting and the imam gestures lying down.
D) When both gesture from a standing position.

Key Takeaway
A mu'mi may follow a mu'mi only when states are equal; the follower must not be in a stronger state than the imam.

Following a Gesturing Imam: The Stronger Cannot Follow the Weaker
Ruling and dispute on following a gesturing imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a fully able person following a gesturing imam and evaluate Imam Zufar's counter-argument using the principle of 'aqwa hal'.

Core Idea
A stronger state cannot follow a weaker state in congregational prayer.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in congregational prayer: when the imam is ill and prays with gestures (e.g., sitting and gesturing for ruku' and sujood), can a follower who is able to perform full ruku' and sujood follow him? The Hanafi school prohibits it, citing the principle that the stronger cannot follow the weaker. Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, disagreed, drawing an analogy to tayammum. We will examine both arguments and understand the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a person who can perform ruku' and sujood (full movements) should not pray behind an imam who only gestures. The text states: 'The one who bows and prostrates does not pray behind the gesturing person.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) holds that the gesturing imam can lead a fully able follower. He argues that the gestures are a substitute (badal) for ruku' and sujood, analogous to tayammum substituting for wudu.
Imam Zufar is known for differing from Abu Hanifa in many matters.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Imam Zufar uses qiyas (analogy): just as a person with tayammum (substitute) can lead a person with water (original), a gesturing imam (substitute) can lead a person who bows (original). The substitute is treated like the original.
This is qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because it involves a subtle principle.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rejects the analogy. Gesture is not a true substitute for ruku' and sujood; it is simply a concession for the incapacitated person. The follower's state is stronger (aqwa), so he cannot follow a weaker state. The principle that the weaker cannot lead the stronger overrides the analogy.
The text says: 'We do not accept that because a gesture is not a substitute for ruku' and sujood; gesture is for both, and some things are not substitutes for others.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, if a fully able person prays behind a gesturing imam, his prayer is invalid (or at least makruh tahrimi). He must repeat it. Imam Zufar would consider it valid.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصلي الذي يركع ويسجد خلف الـمـؤمـى لان حال المقتدى اقوى و فيه خلاف زد تشریح ص ترجمہ اور رکوع اور سجدہ کرنے والا اقتداء نہ کرے اشارہ کرنے والے کے پیچھے کیونکہ مقتدی کی حالت اقوی ہے اور اس میں امام اقتدار عصر کی نمہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ رکوع اور سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنے والا اشارہ کرنے والے کے پیچھے نماز نہ پڑھے۔ امام زفر نے کہا کہ اٹا اس لئے اقتدار کرنے والا رکوع سجدہ کر نیوالے کی امامت کر سکتا ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشارے کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنے والے سے رکوع اور کیا امام شافعی بالبدل ساقط ہو گئے یعنی رکوع اور سجدہ اگر چہ ساقط ہو گئے لیکن ان کا بدل یعنی اشارہ موجود ہے اور بدل کے ساتھ ادا کرنا ایسا ہے جسے ہی ہے اسی طرح مصر کے ساتھ ادا کرنا، یہی وجہ ہے کہ متیم متوخنیقین کی امامت کر سکتا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ میں مقتدی کا حال اقوامی ہے اور امام کا اضعف اور سابق میں یہ اصول گذر چکا ہے کہ اضعف النار کے نزدیک سر اقوامی حال والے کی امامت نہیں کر سکتا۔ رہا یہ کہ اشارہ رکوع اور سجود کا بدل ہے سو ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں کیونکہ اشارہ رکوع اور سجدہ کا بھی ہے اور بعض شئی شئی کا بدل نہیں ہوتا۔
And the one who bows and prostrates does not pray behind the gesturing person because the state of the follower is stronger, and there is a difference of opinion in it. Translation: The one who performs ruku' and sujood should not follow the gesturing person because the follower's state is stronger, and there is a difference of opinion in this. Explanation: The issue is that a person who prays with ruku' and sujood should not pray behind a person who only gestures. Imam Zufar said that the gesturing person can lead the one who bows and prostrates. Imam Zufar's proof is that ruku' and sujood are waived from the gesturing person, but their substitute (badal) - the gesture - exists, and performing with the substitute is like performing with the original, just as a person who performs tayammum can lead a person who has water. Our proof is that in this issue the follower's state is stronger and the imam's is weaker, and the rule passed is that the weaker cannot lead the stronger. As for the claim that gesture is a substitute for ruku' and sujood, we do not accept that because a gesture is not a substitute for ruku' and sujood; gesture is for both, and some things are not substitutes for others.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute, primarily between the Hanafi school and Imam Zufar. The ruling states that a person who can perform ruku' and sujood normally may not follow an imam who prays with gestures, because the follower's state is stronger (aqwa). Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar who often differs) argues that the gesturing imam can lead such a person because the gestures are a substitute (badal) for ruku' and sujood, analogous to tayammum leading someone with water. The Hanafi response rejects this analogy, stating that gesture is not a genuine substitute; rather the gesture replaces the entire action due to necessity, but the weaker state cannot lead the stronger. The passage also mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i (likely) has another view, but the Hanafi position is firmly against it.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): A substitute that stands in place of a primary obligation when it is impossible to perform the original.
اقوی حالت (aqwa hal): A stronger physical state in prayer, such as being able to bow and prostrate compared to gesturing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (excluding Imam Zufar), can a person who performs full ruku' and sujood follow an imam who prays with gestures?
A) Yes, because the imam's gestures are a substitute for ruku' and sujood.
B) No, because the follower's state is stronger than the imam's.
C) Yes, as long as the imam is seated.
D) No, unless the follower also gestures.

Key Takeaway
The principle that a stronger physical state cannot follow a weaker one overrides any analogy to substitutes like tayammum; a fully able person must not follow a gesturing imam.

Ruling on Obligatory Prayer Behind Voluntary Imam
Ruling with ta'lil on muftaridh following mutanafifil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muftaridh following a mutanafifil and explain the legal reasoning based on the concept of bina'.

Core Idea
A fard performer cannot follow a nafl imam because the follower builds upon the imam's prayer.

This lesson addresses a key rule in Hanafi congregational prayer: a person performing an obligatory prayer (muftaridh) cannot validly follow an imam who is performing a voluntary prayer (mutanafifil). The reasoning is grounded in the concept of 'bina'' (building), where the follower's prayer is constructed upon the imam's. We will examine the ruling, its rationale, and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules on a muftaridh (obligatory prayer performer) following a mutanafifil (voluntary prayer performer). The ruling is that it is not permissible—'he does not pray.'
The ruling is clearly stated as a prohibition/invalidity.
2
Extract the reasoning (ta'lil)
The reason given is 'because following (iqtida') is building (bina'), and the description of obligatory-ness (fardiyyah) is absent in the imam, so the building is not realized.'
The word 'lianna' introduces the cause.
3
Explain the concept of bina'
Bina' means that the follower's prayer is built upon the imam's. For the building to stand, the imam's prayer must share the same legal description (wasf) as the follower's—in this case, fardiyyah.
If the imam prays nafl, his prayer lacks fardiyyah, so the follower cannot build a fard prayer upon it.
4
Apply the condition
The implicit condition for valid iqtida' is that the imam's prayer must match the follower's in type (fard or nafl). Failure to meet this condition renders the congregation invalid.
This condition is specific to the Hanafi school.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
While the Hanafi school prohibits this, other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow it under certain circumstances. Recognize this as an area of ikhtilaf.
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصلى المفترض خلف المتنفل لان الاقتداء بناء ووصف الفرضية معدوم فى حق الامام فلا يتحقق البناء حاصل یہ کرے تو گویا دا على المعدوم
And the person performing obligatory prayer does not pray behind the person performing voluntary prayer because following is building (bina'), and the description of obligatory-ness (fardiyyah) is absent in the imam, so the building is not realized. The conclusion: he would be like building upon non-existent.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This is a ruling statement explaining that a person performing an obligatory prayer cannot follow an imam who is performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer. The reasoning is that following an imam (iqtida') is like building (bina') upon someone else's prayer. For the follower's prayer to be valid as an obligatory prayer, the imam's prayer must also be obligatory in description (wasf al-fardiyyah). Since the imam's prayer is voluntary, the necessary condition is absent, so the building fails. The Urdu commentary elaborates that it would be like trying to build on nothing.

Key Terms
مفترض (muftaridh): A person who is performing an obligatory (fard) prayer.
متنفل (mutanafifil): A person who is performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer.
بناء (bina'): Building upon another's prayer, meaning the follower's prayer is contingent on the imam's.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible for a person performing fard prayer to follow an imam performing nafl prayer?
A) Because the imam's prayer is weaker.
B) Because following requires the imam's prayer to also be obligatory in description.
C) Because the follower must intend the same prayer as the imam.
D) Because nafl prayer cannot be performed in congregation.

Key Takeaway
For a valid congregation, the imam and follower must be performing prayers of the same legal type (fard or nafl) because the follower's prayer is built upon the imam's.

Fard Performer Cannot Follow a Nafl or Different Fard Performer
Ruling on fard performer behind nafl or different fard performer, with Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following a nafl or different fard imam, explain the reasoning (bina and tadammun), and compare the Shafi'i position with the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Unity of prayer type is essential for valid iqtida in Hanafi; the follower's prayer is built upon the imam's.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a person praying fard follow an imam praying nafl or a different fard? The Hanafi position is strict—requiring unity of prayer type—based on the concepts of bina (building) and tadammun (incorporation). The Shafi'i school allows it, citing the hadith of Mu'adh. Let's explore the proofs and implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two rulings from the matn: a fard performer cannot follow a nafl performer, and a fard performer cannot follow another fard performer of a different type. Both are invalid (batil).
The Hanafi school requires unity of obligation (ittihad) between imam and follower.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such following is valid in all cases, whether nafl or different fard.
Shafi'i defines iqtida as mere conformity in actions, without partnership in tahrima.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith of Mu'adh, who prayed Isha with the Prophet (as nafl) then led his people in the same prayer (as fard).
This suggests a muftarid can follow a mutanaffil.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) the hadith is ambiguous—Mu'adh may have intended nafl with the Prophet; (2) if such following were valid, the prayer of fear (salat al-khawf) would not have been legislated, as the Prophet could have prayed full prayer with each group instead of splitting.
These responses undermine the Shafi'i inference.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in Hanafi, a follower must be performing the exact same obligatory prayer as the imam; in Shafi'i, any prayer type can follow any other as long as actions match.
E.g., Zuhr cannot follow Asr in Hanafi, but is valid in Shafi'i.

Source Text

باب الامامة
رجمہ [؟] اور فرض ادا کرنے والا نفل ادا کرنے والے کے پیچھے نہ پڑھے کیونکہ اقتداء کرنا بناء ہے حالانکہ عام کے حق میں فرضیت کا وصف معدوم ہے پس اینا [بناء] کرنا معدوم پر متفق نہ ہو گا۔
تشریح: مفترض کے لئے متفل کے اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اقتداء نام ہے بناء کرنے کا اور بناء امر وجودی ہے نہ کہ امر عدمی، اور عدمی اس لئے ہے کہ بناء نام ہے ایک شخص کا دوسرے شخص کی متابعت کرنا اس کے افعال میں مع ان کی صفات کے۔ اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ متابعت مفہوم وجودی ہے نہ کہ مفہوم سلبی، اور امر وجودی کی بنا امر عدمی پر مطابقت نہیں ہے۔ پس چونکہ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں وصف فرضیت لام [؟] کے حق میں معدوم ہے، اس لئے بناء کرنا تحقیق نہیں ہو گا اور جب بناء کرنا تحقیق نہیں ہو تو اقتداء کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہو گا۔
ایک فرض والے کے لئے دوسرے فرض والے کے پیچھے نماز کا حکم
قال ولامن يصلى فرضا خلف من يصلى فرضا آخر لان الاقتداء شركة وموافقة فلابد من الاتحاد وعند الشافعي يصح في جميع ذلك لان الاقتداء عنده اداء على سبيل الموافقة وعندنا معنى التضمن مراعى۔
ترجمہ: اور نہ اقتداء کرے وہ شخص جو فرض پڑھتا ہے پیچھے اس شخص کے جو دوسرا فرض پڑھتا ہے، کیونکہ اقتداء تو شرکت اور موافقت کا نام ہے، اس لئے اتحاد ضروری ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ان سب صورتوں میں اقتداء درست ہے، کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اقتداء علی سبیل الموافقة ادا کرنے کا نام ہے، اور ہمارے نزدیک ضمن [تضمن] کے معنی محفوظ ہیں۔
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک فرض ادا کرنے والا دوسرا فرض ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء نہ کرے مثلاً ظہر کی نماز پڑھنے والا عصر کی نماز پڑھنے والے کے پیچھے جائز نہیں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقتداء نام ہے تحریمہ کے اندر شرکت اور افعال بدنیہ کے اندر متابعت کا۔ اور شرکت میں موافقت اس وقت ہو سکتی ہے جبکہ دونوں کے تحریمہ اور افعال میں اتحاد ہو، اور چونکہ مذکورہ صورت میں اتحاد نہیں، اس لئے اقتداء بھی درست نہیں ہو گی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک مذکورہ تمام صورتوں میں اقتداء درست ہے یعنی رکوع سجدہ کرنے والے، اشارہ کرنے والے کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے، نیز مفترض متفل کی اور ایک فرض ادا کرنے والا دوسرا فرض ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ الاقتداء علی سبیل الموافقة ارکان کے ادا کرنے کا نام ہے یعنی صرف اعمال میں موافقت ہو، پس گویا ان کے نزدیک ہر شخص اپنی نماز ادا کرنے میں منفرد ہے اور جماعت صرف اس قدر ہے کہ افعال جو ہر ایک ادا کرتا ہے وہ ایک ساتھ ادا کریں۔ پس اس دلیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ شوافع کے نزدیک صرف افعال کے اندر موافقت ضروری ہے شرکت فی التحریمہ ضروری نہیں ہے، اور جب شرکت فی التحریمہ ضروری نہیں تو ایک فرض ادا کرنے والا دوسرا فرض ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک موافقت کے ساتھ تضمن کے معنی بھی ملحوظ ہیں یعنی ہاں [یہاں] نماز مقتدی کی نماز کو متضمن ہوتی ہے حتی کہ امام کی نماز فاسد ہونے سے مقتدی کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی اور امام کی نماز کے صحیح ہونے سے مقتدی کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی۔ ضمانت امام کی دلیل حدیث ابو ہریرۃ رضی اللہ عنہ "الامام ضامن" ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ ہمارے نزدیک جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ادا کرنا ایسا ہے جیسے کوئی شخص کچھ لوگوں کی دعوت کرے اور کھانے کا نظم بھی خود کرے تو گویا داعی مدعو حضرات کے کھانے کا ضامن ہو گیا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ادا کرنا ایسا ہے جیسے کچھ لوگ اپنے اپنے گھر سے کھانا لا کر کسی ایک آدمی کے دستر خوان پر جمع ہو کر تناول کر لیں، تو گویا ان کے صرف کھانے میں موافقت پائی گئی، کسی کا ذمہ دار اور ضامن نہیں ہوا۔
امام شافعی کا استدلال اس مسئلہ میں کہ مفترض کی نماز متفل کے پیچھے جائز ہے حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث ہے: معاذا كان يصلي العشاء مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم يرجع فيصليها بقومه في بني سلمة فكان صلاته فرضا وصلاته نفلا۔ یعنی معاذ رضی اللہ عنہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ساتھ عشاء کی نماز پڑھتے تھے پھر واپس جا کر بنو سلمہ میں اپنی قوم کو پڑھاتے تھے، پس معاذ کی قوم کی نماز فرض ہوتی اور معاذ کی نماز نفل ہوتی۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مفترض کی نماز متصل [متفل] کے پیچھے جائز ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہوگا کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ معاذ بہ نیت نفل حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ساتھ نماز پڑھتے ہوں اور اپنی قوم کو نماز فرض پڑھاتے ہوں، پس اس احتمال کے ساتھ امام شافعی کا استدلال درست نہیں ہوگا۔ ہماری طرف سے یہ بھی جواب ہے کہ اگر مفترض کا نفل کے پیچھے اقتداء کرنا جائز ہوتا تو صلوۃ خوف میں یہ طریقہ مشروع نہ ہوتا کہ آدھی نماز ایک طائفہ کو پڑھائے اور آدھی دوسرے طائفہ کو، بلکہ پوری پوری نماز پڑھا دی جاتی۔ چنانچہ یہ بات ثابت ہے کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ہجرت کے ایک زمانہ کے بعد دو گروہوں کو نماز آدھی آدھی پڑھائی اور درمیان میں کچھ نماز کے منافی افعال کرنے پڑے، پس اگر مفترض کے لئے متفل کی اقتداء کرنا درست ہوتا تو آپ ہر گروہ کو پوری نماز پڑھا دیتے، آدھی آدھی نہ پڑھاتے۔
Chapter of Imamate. A man: And the one performing fard should not follow behind the one performing nafl, because following is building (bina'), while the attribute of obligation (fardiyya) is non-existent in the general [nafl], so building cannot be established on the non-existent. Commentary: It is not permissible for a muftarid to follow a mutanaffil, because following is called building, and building is an existential matter, not a non-existential one. And it is non-existential because building is the following of one person to another in his actions along with their attributes, and it is clear that following is an existential concept, not a privative one, and an existential matter cannot be built upon a non-existent one. So since in the mentioned issue the attribute of obligation is non-existent for the follower, building cannot be realized, and when building is not realized, following is not valid. Ruling for one fard behind another fard: He said: And the one who prays fard behind one who prays another fard is not permitted, because iqtida is partnership and conformity, so unity is necessary. According to al-Shafi'i, it is valid in all that, because iqtida in his view is performing in the way of conformity. According to us, the meaning of incorporation (tadammun) is observed. Translation: And the person who prays fard should not follow behind the person who prays a different fard, because iqtida is partnership and conformity, so unity is necessary. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, in all these cases following is valid, because according to him iqtida is performing on the basis of conformity, and according to us the meaning of incorporation is preserved. Commentary: The situation is that one performing fard should not follow another performing a different fard, e.g., one praying Zuhr behind one praying Asr is not valid. The proof: iqtida is partnership in the opening takbir and conformity in physical actions. Partnership requires unity in both. Since there is no unity, following is not valid. According to al-Shafi'i, following is valid in all these cases: one who performs bowing and prostration can follow one who signals; also a muftarid can follow a mutanaffil and one performing one fard can follow another fard. His proof: iqtida is performing actions in conformity, i.e., only conformity in actions. So according to him each person is independent in his own prayer, and congregation is only that they perform actions together. Thus for the Shafi'is, only conformity in actions is necessary, not partnership in the opening takbir. According to us, along with conformity, the meaning of incorporation is also considered: the follower's prayer is incorporated into the imam's, such that the imam's prayer being invalid invalidates the follower's prayer, and the imam's prayer being valid validates the follower's prayer. The proof of the imam's guarantee is the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'The imam is a guarantor.' The conclusion: According to us, praying in congregation is like a person who invites some people and arranges the food himself; the inviter becomes the guarantor of the guests' food. According to al-Shafi'i, praying in congregation is like some people bringing food from their own homes and gathering at one person's table to eat; only conformity in eating is found, no one becomes responsible or guarantor. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence in this issue that a muftarid can follow a mutanaffil is the hadith of Mu'adh: he used to pray Isha with the Prophet, then return and lead his people in Bani Salama, so his prayer was nafl and theirs was fard. This shows that a muftarid can follow a mutanaffil. Our response: It is possible that Mu'adh prayed with the Prophet with the intention of nafl and led his people in fard; this possibility makes the inference invalid. Another response: If it were valid, the prayer of fear would not have been legislated whereby the imam prays half with one group and half with another; instead he would pray the full prayer with each group. It is established that the Prophet after Hijrah led two groups in prayer, half each, and had to perform actions contrary to prayer in between. So if following a mutanaffil were valid, he would have prayed the full prayer with each group, not half.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of following an imam who is performing a different type of prayer. The passage begins by stating two rulings from the matn of al-Hidayah: (1) a person performing an obligatory (fard) prayer may not follow a person performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer; (2) a person performing one fard prayer may not follow a person performing a different fard prayer (e.g., Zuhr behind Asr). The Hanafi position is that such following is invalid (batil). The reasoning is that iqtida (following in prayer) involves two elements: partnership in the opening takbir (tahrima) and conformity in physical actions. Partnership requires that both imam and follower share the same prayer type (same obligation), otherwise there is no unity (ittihad). Furthermore, the Hanafi school incorporates the concept of daman (guarantee): the imam is a guarantor for the follower's prayer, based on the hadith 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor). This implies that the follower's prayer is built upon the imam's; if the imam's prayer is invalid, the follower's is also invalid. Therefore, the imam's prayer must be valid and of the same type. The passage then presents the Shafi'i position, which holds that iqtida is merely performing actions in conformity (ada' ala sabil al-muwafaqa) without requiring unity of prayer type or partnership in tahrima. Shafi'is allow following in all these cases, relying on the hadith of Mu'adh where he prayed Isha with the Prophet (as nafl) and then led his people in the same prayer as fard. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) the hadith is ambiguous—Mu'adh may have intended nafl with the Prophet; (2) if such following were valid, the prayer of fear (salat al-khawf) would not have been prescribed, where the imam splits the prayer into two groups. That practice would be unnecessary if a muftarid could follow a mutanaffil. Thus the Hanafi position is upheld: unity of prayer type is essential. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida): Following the imam in prayer, involving partnership in tahrima and conformity in actions.
بناء (bina): The concept that the follower's prayer is built upon the imam's prayer; a metaphor for dependency.
تضمن (tadammun): The incorporation of the follower's prayer into the imam's; the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, can a person praying Zuhr (fard) follow an imam praying Asr (fard)?
A) Yes, because both are fard prayers.
B) No, because they are different fard prayers and lack unity (ittihad).
C) Yes, as long as the actions are performed together.
D) No, only if the follower also intended Asr.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, iqtida requires unity of prayer type and partnership in tahrima; a fard performer cannot follow a nafl or different fard performer.

Salah — Prayer

Following an Imam Found to Be in Hadath Requires Repetition
Ruling that both imam and followers must repeat prayer if imam is discovered to be in hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repetition of prayer when the imam is discovered to have been in hadath, and explain the concept of tadammun that underlies it.

Core Idea
If the imam's prayer was invalid due to hadath, both he and the followers must repeat — their prayers are incorporated into his.

What happens if you pray behind an imam and later learn he was without wudu or in a state of major impurity? This passage addresses precisely that scenario, ruling that both the imam and the followers must repeat their prayers. The proof lies in a prophetic hadith and the Hanafi principle of tadammun (incorporation), which differs from the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the act of following an imam who is later discovered to have been in hadath. The ruling is that the prayer must be repeated (i'ada) by both the imam and the followers. Determine the hukm level: it is wajib, not merely sunnah.
The imperative form in the hadith indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'Whoever leads a people, then it becomes apparent that he was in hadath, he should repeat his prayer and they should repeat.' Identify this as a dalil naqli (textual proof) of ahad status.
The exact wording includes the command 'اعاد' for both.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative verb ('اعاد') in the hadith is the key. According to Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (a command indicates obligation). Thus, repeating is wajib for both. Also, the inclusion of 'and they repeat' shows the followers are directly addressed.
This reasoning relies on the literal meaning of the text.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage notes that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. Understand that his position is based on a different understanding of iqtida (following the imam) – he sees it as mere conformity, not incorporation. Therefore, he does not require followers to repeat.
The disagreement is rooted in usul al-fiqh: does the follower's prayer 'merge' with the imam's or remain independent?
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the concept of tadammun (incorporation). The imam is a guarantor (damin) for the followers' prayer; if his prayer is invalid, theirs is too. This is the mufta bihi (operative) position, supported by the majority of Hanafi imams.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من اقتدى بامام ثم علم ان امامه محدث اعاد لقوله عليه السلام من ام قوما ثم ظهر انه كان محدثا اعاد صلاته واعادوا وفيه خلاف الشافعي بناء على ما تقدم ونحن تعتبر معنى التضمن وذلك في الفساد والجنابة [؟] فاسد [؟]...
ترجمہ: اور جس نے کسی امام کی اقتداء کی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ اس کا امام محدث ہے تو نماز کا اعادہ کرے، کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا: جس نے کسی قوم کی امامت کی پھر ظاہر ہوا کہ وہ محدث تھا تو وہ اپنی نماز کا اعادہ کرے اور وہ بھی اعادہ کریں۔ اس میں امام شافعی کے ساتھ اختلاف ہے، جیسا کہ پہلے گزرا۔ اور ہم تضمن کے معنی کو معتبر سمجھتے ہیں، اور یہ فساد اور جنابت [؟] میں ہے۔
And whoever follows an imam, then learns that his imam was in hadath (ritual impurity), repeats the prayer, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever leads a people, then it becomes apparent that he was in hadath, he should repeat his prayer and they should repeat.' In it is a difference with al-Shafi'i based on what preceded. And we consider the meaning of incorporation (tadammun), and that is in invalidity and janaba [؟]...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its prophetic proof: if a follower later discovers that the imam was in a state of hadath (ritual impurity, such as without wudu or in major impurity) during the prayer, both the imam and the followers must repeat their prayers. The hadith quoted is: 'Whoever leads a people, then it becomes apparent that he was in hadath, he should repeat his prayer and they should repeat.' This shows the Hanafi principle of tadammun (incorporation): the imam's prayer being invalid due to hadath renders the followers' prayers invalid as well, because the followers' prayers are incorporated into the imam's. The passage notes that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, based on his view that iqtida is only conformity in actions (as explained earlier), so he would not require followers to repeat. However, the Hanafi relied-upon position is that repetition is necessary, as the imam is a guarantor for the followers' prayers.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu or ghusl, such as passing wind, urine, stool, or major impurity like janaba.
اعادہ (i'ada): Repetition of the prayer due to invalidity of the original prayer.
تضمن (tadammun): Incorporation; the Hanafi principle that the follower's prayer is merged with and dependent on the imam's prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the imam must repeat, the followers' prayer is valid.
B) Both the imam and the followers must repeat their prayers.
C) The followers must repeat, but the imam does not.
D) No one needs to repeat if the prayer was completed.

Key Takeaway
If the imam is discovered to have been in hadath (ritual impurity), both he and the followers must repeat their prayers because the followers' prayer is incorporated into the imam's (tadammun).

Muftarid Behind Mutanaffil: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Shafi'i argument and Hanafi response on muftarid behind mutanaffil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muftarid following a mutanaffil and explain the key arguments of both the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
A muftarid cannot follow a mutanaffil in Hanafi fiqh; the hadith of Mu'adh is ambiguous.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: is it valid for a person performing an obligatory prayer (muftarid) to follow an imam performing a supererogatory prayer (mutanaffil)? Imam al-Shafi'i argues in favor using the hadith of Mu'adh, while the Hanafi school responds with a critical analysis of that hadith and a strong analogy from the fear prayer (Salat al-Khawf). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate conflicting proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: a muftarid's prayer behind a mutanaffil is invalid (fasid). This is the mufta bihi view.
The muftarid must repeat the prayer if time remains.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such a prayer is valid. His evidence is the hadith of Mu'adh.
Shafi'i relies on the apparent meaning of the hadith.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Examine the hadith: Mu'adh prayed 'Isha with the Prophet (as a muftarid) and later led his people in the same prayer (now as a mutanaffil). The followers presumably prayed fard behind him.
The hadith is ahad, so zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school poses a possibility: Mu'adh may have intended nafl with the Prophet and fard when leading his people. The hadith is ambiguous. Additionally, if it were valid, the fear prayer (Salat al-Khawf) would not have been split into halves.
The Salat al-Khawf analogy is a rational (qiyas) argument.
5
Determine the practical difference
In practice, a Hanafi follower must avoid praying behind an imam performing nafl; if he does, his prayer is invalid. A Shafi'i follower would consider it valid.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام شافعی کا استدلال اس مسئلہ میں کہ مفترض کی نماز متغفل کے پیچھے جائز ہے حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث ہے معاذا كان يصلى العشاء مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم يرجع فيصليها بقومه في بني سلمة فكان صلاة فرضا و صلاته نفلا یعنی معاذ بن حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ساتھ عشاء کی نماز پڑھتے تھے پھر واپس جا کر بنو سلمہ میں اپنی قوم کو پر کسی قوم کی امامت اختلاف ہے اس۔ تشریح صورت کرے گا اور اگر اقتداء کرنے کے پس معاذ کی قوم کی نماز فرض ہوتی اور معاذ کی نماز نفل ہوتی اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مفترض کی نماز متصل کے پیچھے جائز ہے۔ ان کے نزدیک و ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہوگا کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ معاذ بہ نیت نفل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ نماز پڑھتے ہوں اور اپنی قوم کو فرش مقتدی کی نماز کو ہوں ۔ پس اس احتمال کے ساتھ امام شافعی کا استدلال درست نہیں ہوگا۔ ہماری طرف سے یہ بھی جواب ہے کہ اگر مفترض کا نفل اگر چہ حدث کی تفصیل اس اقتداء کرنا جائز ہوتا تو صلوۃ خوف میں یہ طریقہ مشروع نہ ہوتا کہ آدھی نماز ایک طائفہ کو پڑھائے اور آدھی دوسرے طائفہ کو بلکہ پوری پوری نماز پڑھادی جاتی چنانچہ یہ بات ثابت ہے کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ہجرت کے ایک زمانہ کے بعد دو گروہوں نماز آدھی آدھی پڑھائی اور درمیان میں [؟] وہ کہ نماز کے منافی افعال کرنے پڑے پس اگر مفترض کے لئے متنفل کی اقتداء کر ہی ہے اور یا یہ کہ وہ صحیح ہے پھر اب تو آپ ہر گروہ کو پوری نماز پڑھا دیتے آدھی آدھی نہ پڑھاتے۔
The argument of Imam al-Shafi'i in this issue that the prayer of a muftarid (obligated) behind a mutanaffil (supererogatory) is valid is the hadith of Hadrat Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him): Mu'adh used to pray 'Isha with the Prophet (peace be upon him) then return and lead his people in Banu Salamah, so his prayer was a fard and his prayer was a nafl. That is, Mu'adh bin Jabal used to pray 'Isha with the Prophet, then return and lead his people in Banu Salamah, leading a people. There is a dispute. Explanation of the scenario: He will do, and if after following, Mu'adh's people's prayer was fard and Mu'adh's prayer was nafl. From this hadith it is known that the prayer of a muftarid behind a mutanaffil is valid. According to them, our response is that it is possible Mu'adh prayed with the intention of nafl with the Prophet and led his people with the intention of fard. So with this possibility, Imam Shafi'i's argument is not valid. Another response from us is that if a muftarid following a nafl was valid, then in the prayer of fear (Salat al-Khawf) this method would not have been prescribed: that half the prayer be led for one group and half for the other; rather, the entire prayer would have been offered. Indeed, it is established that the Prophet after the migration led two groups in half-half prayers, and in between actions contrary to prayer had to be performed. So if a muftarid following a mutanaffil is valid and correct, then the Prophet would have led each group in the full prayer, not half-half.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a person performing a fard (obligatory) prayer may follow an imam performing a nafl (supererogatory) prayer. Imam al-Shafi'i argues in favor using the hadith of Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him), where Mu'adh prayed 'Isha with the Prophet (obligatory for him) and then led his people in the same prayer, which for him was nafl. Shafi'i concludes that the muqtadis (followers) prayed fard behind a mutanaffil imam, thus it is valid. The Hanafi school responds by challenging the certainty of this interpretation: Mu'adh may have made his intention nafl when praying with the Prophet and fard when leading his people. Given this possibility, the hadith is not decisive. Additionally, the Hanafis present a rational argument from the practice of Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer), where the Prophet divided the congregation into two groups, each praying half the prayer behind him. If a muftarid could validly follow a mutanaffil, there would have been no need for this division; the Prophet could have led the entire prayer for each group separately. Thus, the Hanafi position is that a muftarid cannot follow a mutanaffil; the prayer would be invalid. The relied-upon view is that of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مفترض (muftarid): One who is performing a fard (obligatory) prayer.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One who is performing a nafl (supererogatory) prayer.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the hadith is weak (da'if)
B) Because Mu'adh may have prayed nafl with the Prophet and fard with his people, making the hadith ambiguous
C) Because the hadith contradicts the Quran
D) Because the hadith was abrogated

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a muftarid cannot validly follow a mutanaffil imam; the hadith of Mu'adh is ambiguous and the fear prayer provides a strong counter-evidence.

Mutanaffil Behind Muftarid: Validity of Following a Fard Imam for Nafl Prayer
Ruling with rational proof for mutanaffil following muftarid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mutanaffil may follow a muftarid imam and explain the proof based on need (hajah) and absolute intention (niat mutlaqah).

Core Idea
A nafl prayer is valid behind a fard imam because the essence of prayer suffices for nafl, and absolute intention covers both.

In the Hanafi school, a person performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer may validly follow an imam who is leading an obligatory (fard) prayer. This may seem counterintuitive since the imam's intention differs from the follower's, but the school's reasoning is grounded in the principle of need (hajah) and the sufficiency of absolute intention. Let's examine the proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Participants
The passage rules that the mutanaffil (one praying nafl) may follow the muftarid (one praying fard) imam. First, identify the two roles: the follower's prayer is nafl, the imam's is fard.
2
Understand the Need (Hajah) of the Mutanaffil
The mutanaffil's requirement is only for the essence of prayer (asl al-salat), not for the specific obligation. This essence—consisting of intention, takbir, qiyam, etc.—exists in the imam's fard prayer as well.
Hajah here refers to the essential need that justifies legal relaxation.
3
Examine the Intention Requirement for Nafl
For a nafl prayer to be valid, an absolute intention (niat mutlaqah) to pray is sufficient. The follower does not need to specify fard or nafl; simply intending to pray is enough.
This contrasts with fard prayer, where specifying fard is required.
4
Connect the Proof
Since the imam's fard prayer includes the essence of prayer and an absolute intention (the imam intends fard, which covers the absolute intention), the mutanaffil's following is valid. The ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) considering the need.
The proof is aqli (rational) rather than naqli (textual).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متنفل کے لئے مفترض کی اقتداء کا حکم ويصلى المتنفل خلف المفترض لان الحاجة في حقه الى اصل الصلوة وهو موجود في حق الامام ترجمہ: اور نماز پڑھے متفل مفترض کے پیچھے کیونکہ متکل کو اصل نماز کی حاجت ہے اور وہ امام کے حق میں موجود ہے۔ تشریح: نفل ادا کرنے والا فرض ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ متصل کے حق میں صرف اصل نماز کی حاجت ہے اور اصل نماز امام کے حق میں بھی موجود ہے اس لئے متفل کا مفترض کے پیچھے اقتداء کرنا محقق ہو جائے گا۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ نفل عنہ صلاۃ درست ہونے کے لئے مطلق نیت کافی ہے اور مطلق نیت پر فرض بھی مشتمل ہے اس لئے اقتداء صحیح ہے۔
The ruling of a mutanaffil following a muftarid: And the mutanaffil prays behind the muftarid because the need for him is for the essence of prayer, and that exists in the right of the imam. Translation: And the mutanaffil prays behind the muftarid because the mutanaffil has need for the essence of prayer, and that exists in the right of the imam. Explanation: The one performing nafl can follow the one performing fard. The evidence is that the mutanaffil only needs the essence of prayer, and the essence of prayer exists in the right of the imam as well, so the mutanaffil's following the muftarid is actualized. The reason is that for the validity of nafl prayer, an absolute intention (niat mutlaqah) is sufficient, and fard also includes absolute intention, so the following is valid.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that a person performing a nafl (supererogatory) prayer may validly follow an imam performing a fard (obligatory) prayer. The proof is based on the concept of need (hajah): the mutanaffil's requirement is simply for the essence of prayer (asl al-salat), which is present in the imam's fard prayer as well. The reasoning is that for a nafl prayer to be valid, an absolute intention (niat mutlaqah) to pray is sufficient; it does not require specification of fard or nafl. Since a fard prayer also contains this absolute intention, the mutanaffil's following is sound. This ruling is well-established in the Hanafi school and is part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
حاجة (hajah): Need; the essential requirement of the mutanaffil for the essence of prayer.
اصل الصلوة (asl al-salat): The essence or reality of prayer, consisting of intention, takbir, qiyam, etc.
نیت مطلقہ (niat mutlaqah): An absolute intention to pray without specifying fard or nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Muqtadi Discovering Imam in Hadath: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on i'adah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires both the imam and muqtadi to repeat their prayers when the imam is discovered to have been in hadath, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The imam is a guarantor of validity: his invalidity invalidates the muqtadi's prayer.

When you pray behind an imam, your prayer is linked to his. But what happens if you find out later that your imam had no wudu? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools reach opposite conclusions. This passage unpacks the proof and reasoning behind the Hanafi position that both must repeat.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school rules: when a muqtadi discovers after prayer that his imam was in hadath, both must repeat (i'adah is wajib).
Note the condition: only discovered after prayer, not before.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State Imam al-Shafi'i's position: the muqtadi's prayer is valid and no repetition is required. Understand his basis: iqtida is conformity, not dependence.
The Shafi'i view makes muqtadi's prayer independent.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the primary evidence: the hadith 'Whoever leads a people... he repeats and they repeat.' Consider why this indicates wujub.
The command is explicit for both.
4
Examine the linguistic analysis of 'al-imam damin'
Follow the Hanafi reasoning: the Prophet's statement 'al-imam damin' is analyzed to mean the imam guarantees validity. Work through the two possibilities and the elimination process.
The analysis narrows it to guarantee of sihha/fasad.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Understand the real-world difference: Hanafi requires both to repeat; Shafi'i only requires the imam to repeat (if at all). Know that the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
This affects actual worship practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی بلکہ مقتدی کی نماز صحیح ہو جائے گی اگر چہ حدث کی وجہ سے امام کی نماز فاسد ہوگئی۔ لیکن ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہوگا کہ ہمارے نزدیک تضمین کے معنی معتبر ہیں۔ تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول الامام ضامن دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ امام اپنی تنہا نماز کا ضامن ہے اور یا یہ کہ اپنی قوم کی نماز کا ضامن ہے پہلی صورت میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ ہر آدمی اپنی نماز کا ضامن ہوتا ہے البتہ دوسری صورت صحیح ہے پھر اب اس کی بھی دو صورتیں ہیں کیونکہ امام اپنی قوم کی نماز کا یا تو وجوب اور اداء ضامن ہو گا یا صحت اور فساد ضامن ہو گا ۔ وجوب اور اداء ضامن ہونا تو بالا جماع مراد نہیں بس متعین ہو گیا کہ صحت اور فساد کے اعتبار سے ضامن ہوتا مراد ہے یعنی امام کی نماز کے صحیح ہونے سے مقتدی کی نماز صحیح ہو جائے گی اور امام کی نماز فاسد ہونے سے مقتدی کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان النبی صلی الله عليه وسلم صلى باصحابه ثم تذكر جنابة فاعادها و قال من ام قوما ثم ظهر انه كان محدثا أو جنبا اعاد صلاته واعادوا یعنی حضور نے اپنے صحابہ کو نماز پڑھائی پھر آپ کو اپنا جنبا ہونا یاد آ گیا تو آپ نے نماز کا اعادہ کیا اور فرمایا کہ جس نے کسی قوم کی امامت کی پھر ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وہ محدث تھا یا جنبی تو وہ اپنی نماز کا اعادہ کرے اور مقتدی لوگ بھی اعادہ کریں۔ اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ امام کی نماز فاسد ہونے مقتدی کی نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے احناف کی تائید میں حضرت جعفر سے حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا فعل روایت کیا ہے ان علیا رضى الله عنه صلى بالناس وهو جنب او على غير وضوء فاعاد و امر هم ان يعيدوا حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ نے لوگوں کو بحالت جنابت یا بغیر وضو نماز پڑھائی پھر نماز کا اعادہ کیا اور لوگوں کو بھی اعادہ کرنے کا حکم کیا اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی کی نماز امام کی نماز کے فاسد ہونے سے فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔
And whoever follows an imam, then knows that his imam was in hadath, he repeats (the prayer) because of his (the Prophet's) saying: 'Whoever leads a people, then it becomes apparent that he was in hadath, he repeats his prayer and they repeat.' And in it there is disagreement with al-Shafi'i based on what preceded. And we consider the meaning of inclusion (tadammun), and that is in validity and invalidity. Explanation of the scenario: If a person follows an imam, then the muqtadi learns that his imam was in hadath, this person will repeat his prayer. And if the imam's state of hadath was known before following, then by consensus following is not permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i said: If after following the imam's hadath becomes known, the muqtadi is not obliged to repeat his prayer. The evidence of Imam al-Shafi'i has passed earlier: according to him, iqtida means performing actions in conformity (ala sabil al-muwafaqat), i.e., the prayers of the imam and muqtadi are separate; the imam's prayer is not included in the muqtadi's prayer. So the invalidity of the imam's prayer does not invalidate the muqtadi's prayer; rather, the muqtadi's prayer is valid even though the imam's prayer became invalid due to hadath. But our response is that we consider the meaning of inclusion (tadammun). Its detail: The Prophet's saying 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor) is not free from two possibilities: either it means the imam is guarantor of his own prayer alone, or he is guarantor of his people's prayer. The first case provides no benefit because every person is guarantor of his own prayer. The second case is correct. Then it has two further possibilities: the imam is guarantor of his people's prayer either in terms of obligation and performance (wujub wa ada) or in terms of validity and invalidity (sihha wa fasad). Being guarantor of obligation and performance is not intended by consensus. So it is determined that he is guarantor in terms of validity and invalidity: when the imam's prayer is valid, the muqtadi's prayer becomes valid, and when the imam's prayer is invalid, the muqtadi's prayer becomes invalid. Our evidence is this hadith: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed with his companions, then he remembered his janabah, so he repeated it and said: Whoever leads a people, then it becomes apparent that he was in hadath or janabah, he repeats his prayer and they repeat.' That is, the Prophet led his companions in prayer, then he remembered he was in janabah, so he repeated the prayer and said that whoever leads a people then it becomes apparent that he was in hadath or junub, he repeats his prayer and the muqtadis also repeat. From this hadith it is established that the invalidity of the imam's prayer invalidates the muqtadi's prayer. 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam narrated in support of the Hanafis from Ja'far from Hadrat Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Ali led the people while he was junub or without wudu, so he repeated and ordered them to repeat.' Hadrat Ali led the people in a state of janabah or without wudu, then he repeated the prayer and ordered them to repeat. From this also it is known that the muqtadi's prayer becomes invalid due to the invalidity of the imam's prayer.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when a muqtadi (follower) discovers after the prayer that his imam was in a state of hadath (ritual impurity, like without wudu or in janabah). The Hanafi school holds that both the imam and the muqtadi must repeat their prayers (i'adah). The Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing that the muqtadi's prayer is independent and thus remains valid. The Hanafi proof is based on the hadith 'Whoever leads a people, then it becomes apparent that he was in hadath or janabah, he repeats his prayer and they repeat.' They also interpret the principle 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor) to mean that the imam is responsible for the validity of the muqtadi's prayer. The passage analyzes the possible meanings of 'damin' to show it refers to guarantee of validity/invalidity, not obligation or performance. Additionally, the action of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) is cited as corroboration. The relied-upon position is the Hanafi view that i'adah is wajib on both.

Key Terms
محدث (muhdith): One who is in a state of minor ritual impurity (i.e., without wudu).
اعادہ (i'adah): Repetition of the prayer due to invalidity.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; here meaning the imam is responsible for the validity of the muqtadi's prayer.
تضمن (tadammun): Inclusion; the idea that the muqtadi's prayer is included in the imam's.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a muqtadi discovers after the prayer that his imam was in a state of hadath?
A) The muqtadi's prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
B) Only the imam must repeat, not the muqtadi.
C) Both the imam and the muqtadi must repeat their prayers.
D) The prayer is invalid but no repetition is required.

Key Takeaway
When the imam is discovered to have been in hadath, the Hanafi school requires both imam and muqtadi to repeat their prayer, based on the hadith and the principle that the imam is guarantor of validity.

Ruling When Imam's Hadath Is Discovered After Prayer
Inter-madhhab dispute on imam's impurity and congregation's prayer repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on repeating prayer when the imam's impurity is discovered, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The imam's impurity invalidates the congregation's prayer due to tadmin (inclusion).

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: when an imam's hadath or janabah is discovered after prayer, does the congregation repeat? The Hanafi school, citing prophetic hadith and the principle of tadmin, obligates both imam and followers to repeat. The Shafi'i school, viewing each prayer as independent, holds only the imam repeats. Understanding this disagreement illuminates core differences in the concept of iqtida'.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: both imam and followers must repeat their prayers. Note the evidence: the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ and the action of 'Ali (ra).
2
Identify the opponent's view
State the Shafi'i position: only the imam repeats; the followers' prayer is valid because each prayer is independent.
Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: iqtida' is mere agreement in actions, not inclusion (tadmin).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Shafi'i reasoning: the imam's invalidity does not transfer to the followers since their prayers are separate.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine how Hanafis rebut: the hadith explicitly commands both to repeat; the principle 'al-imam dhamin' is interpreted as guarantee in validity and invalidity, not just obligation.
The Hanafi analysis of the phrase 'al-imam dhamin' concludes it must refer to validity because obligation aspect adds nothing new.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical consequence: Hanafis require all to repeat; Shafi'is require only the imam to repeat.

باب الامامة
کسی قوم کی امامت کی پھر ظاہر ہوا کہ وہ محدث یا جنبی تھا تو اپنی نماز کا اعادہ کرے اور لوگ اپنی نماز میں اعیادہ کریں اور اس میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس پر بناء کرتے ہوئے جو سابق میں گذر چکا ہے اور ہم مضمون نے معنی کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں اور تضمن جواز اور فساد میں ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے امام کی اقتداء کی پھر مقتدی کو علم ہوا کہ اس کا امام محدث ہے تو یہ شخص اپنی نماز کا اعادہ کرے گا اور اگر اقتداء کرنے سے پہلے ہی امام کا محدث ہونا معلوم ہو گیا تو بالا جماع اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ اگر اقتداء کرنے کے بعد امام کا محدث ہونا معلوم ہوا تو مقتدی پر اپنی نماز کا اعاد دوا جب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی کہ ان کے نزدیک علی سبیل الموافقت افعال ادا کرنے کا نام اقتداء ہے یعنی امام اور مقتدی میں سے ہر ایک کی نماز علیحدہ علیحدہ ہے امام کی نماز مقتدی کی نماز کو ضمن نہیں ہے اس لئے امام کی نماز فاسد ہونے سے مقتدی کی نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی بلکہ مقتدی کی نماز صحیح ہو جائے گی اگر چہ حدث کی وجہ سے امام کی نماز فاسد ہوگئی۔ لیکن ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہوگا کہ ہمارے نزدیک تضمین کے معنی معتبر ہیں۔ تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول الامام ضامن دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ امام اپنی تنہا نماز کا ضامن ہے اور یا یہ کہ اپنی قوم کی نماز کا ضامن ہے پہلی صورت میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ ہر آدمی اپنی نماز کا ضامن ہوتا ہے البتہ دوسری صورت صحیح ہے پھر اب اس کی بھی دو صورتیں ہیں کیونکہ امام اپنی قوم کی نماز کا یا تو جو با اور اداء ضامن ہو گا مہینہ اور فساد اضامن ہو گا ۔ وجو ہا اور اداء ضامن ہونا تو بالا جماع مراد نہیں بس متعین ہو گیا کہ صحت اور فساد کے اعتبار سے ضامن ہوتا مراد ہے یعنی امام کی نماز کے صحیح ہونے سے مقتدی کی نماز صحیح ہو جائے گی اور امام کی نماز فاسد ہونے سے مقتدی کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
ہماری دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان النبی صلی الله عليه وسلم صلى باصحابه ثم تذكر جنابة فاعادها و قال من ام قوما لم ظهرانه كان محدثا اور جنبا اعاد صلاته واعا دو الیعنی حضور نے اپنے صحابہ کو نماز پڑھائی پھر آپ کو اپنا جنین ہوتا یاد آ گیا تو آپ نے نماز کا اعادہ کیا اور فرمایا کہ جس نے کسی قوم کی امامت کی پھر ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وہ محدث تھا یا جنبی تو وہ اپنی نماز کا اعادہ کرے اور مقتدی لوگ بھی اعادہ کریں۔ اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ امام کی نماز فاسد ہونے مقتدی کی نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے احناف کی تائید میں حضرت جعفر سے حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا فعل روایت کیا ہے ان علیا رضى الله ز کے عنه صلى بالناس وهو جنب او على غير وضوء فاعاد و امر هم ان يعيد وا حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ نے لوگوں کو بحالت جنابت یا بغیر وضو نماز پڑھائی پھر نماز کا اعادہ کیا اور لوگوں کو بھی اعادہ کرنے کا حکم کیا اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی کی نماز امام کی نماز کے فاسد ہونے سے فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔
Chapter of Imamate: If someone leads a people in prayer, then it becomes apparent that he was in a state of hadath or junub, he should repeat his prayer and the people should repeat their prayer, and in this Imam Shafi'i has a disagreement, based on what has preceded, and we (Hanafis) consider the meaning of inclusion (tadmin) in validity and invalidity. Explanation: The scenario is that if a person follows an imam, then the follower learns that his imam was in hadath, then this person (the follower) should repeat his prayer. But if the imam's hadath was known before following, then by consensus it is not permissible to follow. Imam Shafi'i said that if after following the imam's hadath becomes known, then repeating the prayer is not obligatory upon the follower. Imam Shafi'i's proof has preceded: according to him, following (iqtida') is performing actions in consensus, i.e., each of the imam and follower has a separate prayer; the imam's prayer does not include the follower's prayer; so the invalidity of the imam's prayer does not invalidate the follower's prayer; rather the follower's prayer becomes valid even if the imam's prayer was invalidated by hadath. But our response is that we consider the meaning of inclusion (tadmin) as valid. Its detail is that the Prophet's ﷺ saying 'The imam is a guarantor (dhamin)' is free from two states: either it means that the imam is guarantor for his own prayer alone or that he is guarantor for his people's prayer. The first case yields no benefit because every person is guarantor for his own prayer. So the second case is correct. Then this also has two states: the imam is guarantor for his people's prayer either in terms of obligation and performance or in terms of validity and invalidity. It is not intended by consensus that he is guarantor in obligation and performance, so it is determined that 'guarantor' means in terms of validity and invalidity, i.e., if the imam's prayer is valid, the follower's prayer becomes valid; and if the imam's prayer is invalid, the follower's prayer becomes invalid. Our proof is this hadith: 'The Prophet ﷺ led his companions in prayer, then remembered he was in a state of janabah, so he repeated the prayer and said: Whoever leads a people in prayer, then it becomes apparent that he was in hadath or junub, he should repeat his prayer and they should repeat.' This proves that the invalidity of the imam's prayer invalidates the follower's prayer. Allamah Ibn al-Humam narrated in support of the Hanafis from Ja'far the action of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Ali led the people while he was junub or without wudu, so he repeated the prayer and ordered them to repeat.' This also shows that the follower's prayer is invalidated by the invalidity of the imam's prayer.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling when an imam's state of ritual impurity (hadath or janabah) is discovered after the prayer has been performed. The Hanafi position is that both the imam and the followers must repeat their prayers, because the imam's prayer is a guarantor (dhamin) for the followers' prayer in terms of validity. The Shafi'i school holds that the followers' prayer remains valid because each person's prayer is independent. The Hanafi argument is based on the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) and the practice of 'Ali (ra). The commentary explains that the term 'tadmin' (inclusion) means that the imam's prayer encompasses the followers' prayer in terms of correctness and invalidity. The author refutes the Shafi'i view by analyzing the meaning of 'al-imam dhamin' and concludes that since the imam is guarantor for the congregation's prayer, his invalidity necessitates theirs.

Key Terms
امام (imam): The person leading the congregation in prayer.
محدث (muhdith): A person who has nullified his wudu (minor impurity).
جنبی (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
تضمین (tadmin): The legal principle that the imam's prayer includes and guarantees the followers' prayer in terms of validity and invalidity.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer by performing actions in conformity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person prays behind an imam and later discovers that the imam had nullified his wudu before the prayer?
A) Only the imam must repeat his prayer
B) Both the imam and the followers must repeat their prayers
C) The prayer is valid for everyone because the followers were unaware
D) The followers should repeat but the imam does not need to

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates both imam and followers to repeat prayer when the imam's impurity is discovered, due to the principle of tadmin (inclusion), which the Shafi'i school rejects.

Ummi Leading Mixed Congregation: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Explaining Abu Hanifa's ruling and Sahibayn's ikhtilaf on ummi as imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa invalidates all prayers when an ummi leads a mixed congregation and evaluate the Sahibayn's contrary analogy.

Core Idea
An ummi imam who can acquire recitation by following a reciter is not excused; his prayer invalidates all via tadmin.

In the previous lesson, we learned the principle of tadmin—that the imam's prayer includes the followers' in validity. Now we apply it to a contested case: an ummi (someone who cannot recite Qur'an) leading a congregation that includes both reciters and other illiterates. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ sharply. Understanding their arguments reveals how the school reasons through analogy (qiyas) and the limits of excuse (udhr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
State the case: an ummi imam (cannot recite Qur'an properly) leads a congregation that includes both reciters (qurra') and illiterate persons (ummiyun). Then note that Abu Hanifa rules all prayers invalid, while the Sahibayn rule the imam's and illiterate followers' prayers valid, but reciters' prayers invalid.
The Sahibayn's position is also within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's analogy to the naked imam
The Sahibayn analogize the ummi imam to a naked imam leading both naked and clothed people. In that case, the naked imam and naked followers are excused (they cannot cover), so their prayers are valid; but the clothed followers' prayers are invalid because they could cover themselves. Similarly, they argue, the ummi imam and illiterate followers are excused from recitation, so their prayers are valid, but reciters are not excused.
This is a qiyas with the naked imam as aṣl (original case).
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's refutation of the analogy
Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy because the ummi imam has a way to become capable of recitation: he could have followed a reciter in prayer (i.e., led but actually followed a reciter in his congregation), which would make the reciter's recitation count as his own. Since he chose not to, he is not excused; he abandoned the obligatory recitation despite ability. Thus his prayer is invalid, and by tadmin, all are invalid.
The key distinction: the naked imam has no ability to cover himself, but the ummi imam has ability to acquire valid recitation through iqtida' (following).
4
Identify the ḥanamāh al-khilāf (practical consequence)
According to Abu Hanifa, the entire congregation must repeat their prayers. According to the Sahibayn, only the reciters repeat; the imam and illiterate followers do not.
This difference matters in daily practice when choosing an imam for a mixed group.
5
Determine the muftā bihī (relied-upon position)
The text indicates that Abu Hanifa's position is generally supported because the imam had ability but abandoned recitation. The muftā bihī is that all prayers are invalid.
Later Hanafi works (like al-Hidayah) uphold Abu Hanifa's view due to the principle of tadmin and the imam's responsibility.

Source Text
