Hadath After Tashahhud and Completion of Prayer
Ruling on hadath after tashahhud with two scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for both involuntary and intentional hadath after tashahhud and explain why repetition is not required.

Core Idea
Hadath after tashahhud does not invalidate the prayer; involuntary requires wudu for salam, intentional completes the prayer.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common concern: what happens if a person experiences ritual impurity (hadath) in the final sitting of prayer, after tashahhud but before salam? The Hanafi school distinguishes between involuntary and intentional hadath, providing clear guidance that preserves the validity of the prayer while maintaining the requirement of purity for the concluding salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) hadath occurs involuntarily after tashahhud, and (2) the person intentionally commits hadath, speaks, or does an action contrary to prayer.
2
State the ruling for involuntary hadath
For involuntary hadath, the person must perform wudu (renew purity) and then say salam. This is because salam is wajib and requires a state of purity.
3
State the ruling for intentional hadath/speech/action
If the person intentionally commits hadath, speaks, or performs a nullifying action, the prayer is considered complete immediately, and no salam is needed. No repetition is required.
4
Analyze the rationale
For intentional nullification: the nullifier (qati') prevents building upon the prayer (al-bina' muta'addhir), but since all integral pillars (arkan) have been performed, the prayer is valid and complete. The salam is a wajib that is waived because the person deliberately ended the prayer.
5
Contrast with general rule
Normally, hadath invalidates prayer. However, after tashahhud, the arkan are complete, so the ruling is exceptional: voluntary nullification ends the prayer without penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان سبقه الحدث بعد التشهد توضأ وسلم لان التسليم واجب فلابد من التوضى ليأتي به. وان تعمد الحدث في هذه الحالة او تكلم او عمل عملا ينافي الصلوة، تمت صلوته لانه تعذر البناء لوجود القاطع لكن لا اعادة عليه لانه لم يبق عليه شيء من الاركان.
ترجمہ: اور اگر مصلی کو تشہد کے بعد حدث ہو گیا تو وضو کر کے سلام پھیرے کیونکہ سلام پھیرنا واجب ہے پس وضو کرنا ضروری ہوا تا کہ سلام پھیرے۔ اور اگر اس نے اس حالت میں عمداً حدث کر دیا یا کلام کیا یا کوئی ایسا عمل کیا جو منافی صلاۃ ہے تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو گئی کیونکہ قاطع پائے جانے کی وجہ سے بناء کرنا متعذر ہو گیا لیکن اس پر نماز کا اعادہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس پر ارکان میں سے کوئی چیز باقی نہیں رہی۔
And if hadath overtakes him after tashahhud, he performs wudu and says salam because salam is obligatory, so wudu is necessary to perform it. And if he intentionally commits hadath in that state, or speaks, or performs an action contrary to prayer, his prayer is complete because building (upon it) is impossible due to the presence of a nullifier, but there is no repetition upon him because no part of the pillars remains upon him.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios after tashahhud (the final sitting before salam). The first: if a person experiences ritual impurity (hadath) involuntarily after tashahhud, he must perform wudu and then say salam. The reason: salam is a wajib act, and since wudu is required for any prayer act after hadath, he must renew wudu to validly say salam. This applies even though the prayer is almost complete; the salam must be performed in a state of purity. The second scenario: if the person intentionally commits hadath, speaks, or does an action that invalidates prayer (like turning away from qiblah), the prayer is considered complete immediately without needing to say salam. Why? Because the nullifier (qati') has occurred, so it is not possible to continue and 'build upon' the prayer (al-bina' muta'addhir). However, there is no obligation to repeat the prayer because all the integral pillars (arkan) have already been performed; only salam remains, and salam is not a pillar but a wajib. Since the person intentionally terminated the prayer, salam is waived? Actually, the text says no repetition is needed because no pillar remains. The Hanafi position: the prayer is valid and complete, and the nullifier effectively ends the prayer. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) indicating that after tashahhud one may stand up if he wishes, implying the prayer's essential part is done. The third scenario: tayammum seeing water during prayer invalidates the prayer, as previously stated. This is a separate ruling: if a mutayammim sees water during prayer, his prayer is batil because the condition of tayammum (lack of water) is no longer met.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity (minor or major) that invalidates wudu or requires ghusl.
تحليل (tahlil): The act of ending the prayer (with salam) to become halal (permissible) to do otherwise forbidden things.
تشہد (tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (al-tahiyyat) in the final sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person intentionally commits hadath after tashahhud, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) He must perform wudu and say salam.
C) The prayer is complete and no repetition is required.
D) He must restart the current rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
Hadath after tashahhud does not invalidate the prayer; involuntary requires wudu for salam, intentional completes the prayer without repetition.

Imam May Not Appoint Successor After Minimum Recitation
Ruling with proof about istihlāf after minimum qirāʾah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an imam appointing a successor after completing the minimum recitation and explain why it invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
No need for a successor once the minimum recitation is complete; doing so invalidates the prayer.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in congregational prayer: the imam has recited the minimum Quran required (one verse or three verses) but then loses the ability to continue. Many assume he can appoint someone else to finish, but the Hanafi school rules that this is impermissible and even invalidates the prayer. We will examine the reasoning based on necessity (ḍarūrah) and its absence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act being ruled upon is the imam appointing a successor (khalīfah) after having recited the minimum amount of Quran that suffices for the prayer. The ruling is that it is not permissible (lā yajūz), and if done, the prayer becomes invalid (fāsid).
2
Note the intra-madhhab difference on the minimum
The minimum recitation (mā yujzī bihī al-ṣalāh) is one verse according to Abu Hanifa, and three verses according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). The ruling applies once either minimum is reached.
This difference does not affect the outcome; both agree that once the minimum is met, appointing a successor is invalid.
3
Understand the proof (dalīl)
The proof is rational: since the purpose of recitation is fulfilled, there is no necessity (ḍarūrah) to change the imam. Without a legitimate religious need, changing the imam is an innovation that invalidates the prayer.
The text claims this ruling is by consensus (bil-ijmāʿ).
4
Contrast with the case where necessity exists
If the imam becomes unable to recite before completing the minimum (e.g., he has not yet recited one verse), then appointing a successor is permissible because there is a genuine need to complete the recitation.
This contrast helps clarify the scope of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر امام ما یجوز بہ الصلوۃ قرآت کر چکا یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک ایک آیت اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تین آیتیں قرآت کر چکا پھر قرآت کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا تو اس کو خلیفہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر اس نے کسی کو خلیفہ کر دیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ یہ حکم بالا جماع ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب مايجوز بہ الصلوۃ قرآن کی قرآت کر لی تو اب خلیفہ بنانے کی کوئی ضرورت باقی نہیں رہی اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ بلا ضرورت شرعی خلیفہ کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
Explanation: If the imam has recited the minimum amount that suffices for prayer—that is, one verse according to Imam Abu Hanifa and three verses according to the Two Companions—and then becomes unable to recite, then appointing a successor is not permissible, and if he appoints a successor, the prayer becomes invalid. This ruling is by consensus. The proof is that once he has recited the minimum required from the Quran, there remains no need to appoint a successor, and it is evident that appointing a successor without a legitimate religious need is not correct.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof concerning an imam who, after completing the minimum recitation required for the validity of prayer, becomes unable to continue recitation. According to the Hanafi school, the minimum recitation is one verse (Abu Hanifa) or three verses (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). If the imam is unable to recite further, he cannot appoint another person to take over as imam (khalifa). If he does so, the prayer is invalidated. The reason is that the purpose of recitation has already been fulfilled, and there is no necessity to change the imam. The ruling is stated to be unanimous (bil-ijma'), and the proof is rational: necessity is absent, so the action is impermissible.

Key Terms
ما يجزئ به الصلاة (mā yujzī bihī al-ṣalāh): The minimum amount of Quranic recitation that suffices for the prayer to be valid.
خليفة (khalīfah): A person appointed by the imam to complete the prayer in his place due to an impediment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, because the minimum recitation is already done, so it is unnecessary.
C) Yes, but only if he is leading a congregation.
D) No, because he must recite at least three verses.

Key Takeaway
An imam who has recited the minimum Quran cannot appoint a successor; doing so invalidates the prayer due to the absence of necessity.

Hadath After Tashahhud: Renew Wudu Then Salaam
Ruling for a person who has a hadath after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a person who experiences hadath after tashahhud and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) that requires wudu before salam.

Core Idea
Salam is wajib; hadath breaks purity, so wudu is needed to perform it validly.

We all strive to complete our prayer perfectly. But what if you lose your wudu after the final sitting (tashahhud) but before the final salam? Does the entire prayer collapse? This short but powerful ruling from the Hanafi school shows how the obligation (wujub) of salam determines the cure: renew wudu, then say salam. The prayer remains valid because the most essential parts have been performed while pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing the final salam after hadath occurred in tashahhud. The ruling is: he must make wudu and then say salam. This is not an optional extra; it is a legal requirement.
2
Recognize the ruling level of salam
In the Hanafi school, salam (taslim) is wajib (obligatory), not a rukn (pillar). This means omitting it intentionally invalidates the prayer, but if forgotten, it can be compensated with sajdah al-sahw. Here, the obligation remains; it hasn't been performed yet.
3
Identify the 'illa (legal cause)
The text explicitly gives the reason: 'because salam is wajib'. The 'illa is the wajib nature of salam. Since hadath invalidates wudu, and salam (an obligatory act) requires purity, the person must restore purity before completing the wajib.
4
Apply the ruling to the scenario
Hadath after tashahhud does not invalidate the entire prayer. It only breaks the state of purity required for the remaining wajib act (salam). Therefore, the person simply renews wudu and then performs salam. The prayer is not repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان سبقه الحدث بعد التشهد توضأ وسلم لان التسليم واجب فلابد من التوضى ليأتي به رجمہ اور اگر مصلی کو تشہد کے بعد حدث ہو گیا تو وضو کر کے سلام پھیرے کیونکہ سلام پھیر نا واجب ہے پس وضو کرنا ضروری ہوا تا کہ سلام پھیرے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کسی نمازی کو تشہد کے بعد حدث ہوا تو حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ وضو کرے اور پھر سلام پھیرے کیونکہ تعلیم واجب ہے پس ال و جب سے وضو کرنا ضروری ہوا تا کہ وجوب سلام ادا کرے۔
And if he is overtaken by hadath after tashahhud, he should perform wudu and say salam, because saying salam is obligatory, so wudu is necessary to perform it. Translation: 'And if a worshipper has hadath after tashahhud, he should do wudu and then say salam, because saying salam is obligatory, so wudu became necessary so that he may say salam.' Explanation: The ruling is that if a worshipper has hadath after tashahhud, he should do wudu and then say salam, because tahlil (saying salam) is wajib, so wudu is necessary to fulfill the obligation of salam.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for a person who experiences a hadath (ritual impurity, like passing wind) after sitting for tashahhud in prayer but before saying salam. According to the Hanafi school, salam is a wajib (obligatory) element of the prayer. Since the person has not yet completed the prayer (salam is still due), if hadath occurs, the state of purity is broken. Therefore, he must make a new wudu (ablation) and then say salam. The proof is that salam is wajib, and the obligation of wudu arises because the act of salam is conditional upon purity.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity, specifically minor impurity (like passing wind, urine, etc.) that breaks wudu.
تشهد (tashahhud): The final sitting in prayer where the testimony of faith is recited.
تسليم (taslīm): Saying salam (al-salamu alaykum) to exit the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person experiences hadath after tashahhud but before saying salam, what should he do?
A) The prayer is invalid, and he must repeat it entirely.
B) He should say salam immediately without wudu.
C) He should perform wudu and then say salam.
D) He should perform tayammum and then say salam.

Key Takeaway
Hadath after tashahhud does not invalidate the prayer; simply renew wudu and say salam, because salam is wajib and requires purity.

Intentional Invalidator After Tashahhud: Prayer Complete
Ruling for intentional hadath/speech after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a worshipper intentionally invalidates prayer after tashahhud, and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, an intentional invalidator ends the prayer—no repetition needed.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in salah: what happens if a person, after completing the tashahhud (the final sitting), intentionally breaks his prayer by committing hadath, speaking, or any act inconsistent with prayer. The Hanafi school holds that the prayer is complete and valid, without requiring repetition. This seems counterintuitive—how can an intentional invalidation not necessitate a repeat? The key lies in the fact that all essential pillars (arkan) have already been performed. Only the salam (exit) remains as wajib. Let's explore the reasoning and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate what the passage rules upon: intentional hadath, speech, or an act contrary to prayer after tashahhud. The ruling is that the prayer is complete (tammat) and no repetition is required.
The passage explicitly states 'تمت صلوته' (his prayer is complete).
2
Understand the condition: tashahhud has been completed
The ruling only applies after the final tashahhud. Before the tashahhud, an intentional invalidator would nullify the prayer entirely.
Tashahhud is the final sitting; after it, only the salam remains.
3
Explore the concept of qāṭiʿ and binā'
The passage says building upon the prayer (binā') is impossible due to the qāṭiʿ (breaker). Once a deliberate invalidator occurs, you cannot continue the prayer. However, because all pillars are done, the prayer is considered concluded.
Binā' is normally allowed for doubts, but not with intentional breakers.
4
Note the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
The hadith indicates that after tashahhud, one may stand up (an action contrary to prayer). This shows that the prayer is essentially complete, and such an action does not require repetition.
The hadith is cited as evidence that the rukn of sitting is over.
5
Conclude the practical effect
Since no rukn remains, there is no obligation to repeat the prayer. The intentional invalidator serves as an unintended way of exiting the prayer, albeit without the ideal salam.
The tahlil (exiting) is achieved through the invalidator itself.

وان تعمد الحدث في هذه الحالة او تكلم او عمل عملا ينافي الصلوة، تمت صلوته لانه تعذر البناء لوجود القاطع لكن لا اعادة عليه لانه لم يبق عليه شيء من الاركان ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے اس حالت میں عمد أحدث کر دیا یا کلام کیا یا کوئی ایسا عمل کیا جو منافی صلاۃ ہے تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو گئی کیونکہ ناٹا پائے جانے کی وجہ سے بناء کرنا مستعد رہے لیکن اس پر نماز کا اعادہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس پر ارکان میں سے کوئی چیز باقی نہیں رہی۔ شریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر تشہد کے بعد مصلی نے عمد احدث کر دیا یا عمدا کلام کیا یا کوئی ایسا کام کیا جو نماز کے منافی ہے تو اس کی نماز پارہ ہوگئی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاطع نماز کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے بناء کرنا تو متعذر ہو گیا لیکن اس پر نماز کا اعادہ بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ارکان میں سےاس پر کوئی چیز باقی نہیں رہی۔ اور رہی تحلیل یعنی خروج بصنعہ سوعمد افعل سے وہ بھی پائی گئی اگر چہ لفظ سلام کے ساتھ تحلیل واجب تھی لیکن اس سے اوپر کے ارکان میں کچھ فساد نہیں ہوتا اور عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کی ظاہر حدیث ( جس میں تشہد ختم کر کے فرمایا کہ تیر اگر کھڑا ہونے کو جی چاہے تو تو کھڑا ہو جا) بھی اس کی مقتضی ہے۔
And if he intentionally commits hadath in this state, or speaks, or does an act contrary to prayer, his prayer is complete because building upon it is impossible due to the existence of a cutter (qāṭiʿ), but there is no repetition upon him because nothing of the pillars remains upon him. Translation: 'And if he in this state intentionally commits hadath or speaks or does an act that is contrary to prayer, then his prayer is complete because building upon it is prevented by the presence of a breaker, but there is no repetition upon him because nothing of the pillars remains upon him.' Explanation: The ruling is that if after tashahhud a worshipper intentionally has hadath or speaks or does something that invalidates prayer, his prayer is concluded. The proof is that because a breaker (qāṭiʿ) occurred, it is impossible to continue the prayer (binā'), but there is no need to repeat the prayer because no essential part (rukn) remains to be performed. As for taḥlīl (exiting the prayer), it is achieved through his intentional act, even though it was obligatory to exit through the words of salam—but this does not nullify the previous pillars. And the apparent hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (when he said after tashahhud: 'If you wish, you may stand up') also indicates this.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
The ruling covers a scenario where a person intentionally nullifies his prayer after tashahhud by committing a hadath, speaking, or doing an act contradictory to prayer (e.g., walking). The Hanafi position is that the prayer is considered complete (tammat) because the essential elements (arkān) have already been performed; only the salam remains, which is wajib. Since the person intentionally broke the continuity, the prayer is concluded by that action itself (as a form of exiting, but not ideal). There is no obligation to repeat the prayer because there is no incomplete rukn. The proof includes a hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) indicating that after tashahhud, one may even stand up, implying that the prayer is near completion.

Key Terms
قاطع (qāṭiʿ): An element that cuts the prayer, like intentional hadath or speech, which breaks the continuity.
بناء (binā'): The concept of continuing prayer by joining the next rakʿah or action after a break; here it is impossible due to the breaker.
تحلیل (taḥlīl): Exiting the state of prayer, normally by saying salam.

D) He must perform wudu and say salam.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, intentional invalidation completes the prayer; no repetition is required because no rukn remains.

Twelve Cases After Tashahhud: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on twelve post-tashahhud events

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on twelve post-tashahhud events, explain the underlying principle (khuruj), and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, Abu Hanifa says events invalidate; Sahibayn say prayer is complete — all because exiting is fard only to Abu Hanifa.

In this passage, Imam al-Hidayah presents a well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: twelve specific events that may occur after the final tashahhud but before salam. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, any of these events invalidates the prayer, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that the prayer remains complete and valid. The difference stems from a fundamental usul principle: whether the voluntary act of exiting the prayer (khuruj) is a fard obligation. Understanding this dispute will sharpen your grasp of how a single theoretical difference can generate multiple practical rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and the Two Positions
Note that the passage describes twelve distinct events that can occur after sitting for tashahhud. The ruling hinges on whether the prayer is still in progress or nearly complete. Abu Hanifa rules the prayer invalid (bāṭil); Sahibayn rule it complete (tammat).
The twelve cases include seeing water (for mutayammim), expiry of mas'h period, removing khuff, an ummi learning a surah, a naked person finding clothes, etc. — all after sitting for tashahhud.
2
Understand the Underlying Principle: Khuruj as Fard
The text explicitly states that the difference originates from whether exiting the prayer by one's own voluntary act (khurūj) is fard. For Abu Hanifa, it is fard; therefore, until salam, the prayer is still in progress and any invalidating event nullifies it. For Sahibayn, khuruj is not fard; the prayer is considered nearly complete after tashahhud, so these events are like occurrences after salam.
This is a classic example of how a usul principle (definition of fard vs. not fard directly affects multiple furu' rulings.
3
Examine the Evidence: Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
The Sahibayn support their position with the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, which indicates that after tashahhud the prayer is essentially complete. The phrase 'tammat salatuh' (his prayer is complete) is interpreted by them as 'near completion' (qārabat al-tamām). Abu Hanifa's proof is logical: whatever is necessary to reach an obligation (here, exiting to pray another prayer) becomes obligatory itself.
The text does not quote the full hadith but alludes to it. The reasoning is a blend of textual and rational arguments.
4
Identify the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
In each of the twelve cases, the consequence differs: under Abu Hanifa's view, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. Under Sahibayn's view, the prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
For example, a mutayammim who sees water after tashahhud: Abu Hanifa requires him to break the prayer and perform wudu; Sahibayn say he may complete the prayer.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi Position
Although the passage presents both views without explicit tarjih, later Hanafi practice generally follows the Sahibayn's view (the prayer is complete) in these specific cases, especially when the event is not volitional or is minor. The fatwa is on the side of ease unless the event is deliberate.
This aligns with the Hanafi tendency to adopt the more lenient view in matters of prayer validity, as long as the core pillars are intact.

Then the prayer is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: his prayer is complete. And it is said that the principle in this is that exiting from the prayer by one's own voluntary act is fard according to Abu Hanifa and not fard according to them. So the occurrence of these impediments in this state is, in his view, like their occurrence during the prayer; and in their view, like their occurrence after salam. For them, we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'He cannot perform another prayer except by exiting from this one. And that without which the obligation cannot be reached is obligatory.' And the meaning of 'tammat' (complete) is 'qārabat al-tamām' (near completion). And appointing a successor is not invalidating, such that it is permissible for a reciter. Rather, the invalidity is due to a necessary ruling, namely the lack of qualification for imamah. Explanation: This passage mentions twelve cases (masa'il ithnashara) that occur after sitting for the extent of tashahhud: 1) The mutayammim sees water. 2) The one wiping over khuff has his wiping period expire. 3) He removes his khuff with a light action. ... Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a major intra-Hanafi dispute concerning twelve specific events that can occur after a person has sat for tashahhud (i.e., after the final sitting but before salam). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, all these events invalidate the prayer (bāṭil), while according to the Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the prayer is considered complete (tāmm). The rationale is a difference in legal theory: Abu Hanifa holds that exiting the prayer is a fard (obligation) that must be done by one's own volition (saying salam). Therefore, if an event that would ordinarily nullify the prayer occurs before the formal exit, the prayer is invalid. The Sahibayn argue that exiting is not a fard in itself; the prayer is considered nearly complete after tashahhud, so these events are like occurrences after salam, and the prayer is valid. They cite the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. The text also clarifies that the word 'tammat' means 'near complete' (qārabat al-tamām). The twelve cases include: seeing water (for mutayammim), expiry of mas'h duration, removing khuff, an ummi learning a surah, a naked person finding clothing, a gesturing person becoming able to bow, remembering a missed prayer, the imam having hadath and appointing an ummi, sunrise in Fajr, Asr time entering during Friday prayer, the jabbirah falling off, and the cessation of a chronic excuse like istihadah. The commentary then lists them in Urdu, though the list is incomplete in the OCR. The overall lesson teaches that the Hanafi school has a nuanced view on what invalidates prayer after tashahhud, with a clear ikhtilaf between the founder and his leading students.

Key Terms
خروج (khurūj): Exiting the state of prayer, normally by saying salam. Abu Hanifa considers it a fard; Sahibayn do not.
تامت صلوته (tammat ṣalātuh): His prayer is complete (in Sahibayn's view). The text explains it means 'near completion' (qārabat al-tamām).
فائتة (fā'itah): A missed prayer that must be made up (qadā). Here it refers to remembering a missed prayer during current prayer after tashahhud.
جبيرة (jabbīrah): A bandage or splint used for a wound, over which mas'h (wiping) is permitted instead of washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He must repeat only the final tashahhud.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, the Sahibayn's view (mufta bihi) is that twelve common events do not invalidate the prayer, based on the principle that khuruj is not fard and the prayer is near completion.

The Final Tashahhud: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Twelve Cases
Lists twelve events after tashahhud and the intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding events after the final tashahhud and apply the underlying principle (khuruj min al-salah as fard or not) to any similar case.

Core Idea
After final tashahhud, prayer is nearly complete for Abu Hanifa, fully complete for Sahibayn — a single word's interpretation changes the ruling on twelve cases.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents twelve specific events that may occur after a worshipper has sat for the duration of the tashahhud in the final sitting. The ruling on whether these events invalidate the prayer or leave it complete depends on a foundational principle: is exiting the prayer by one's own action an obligatory element (fard) or not? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on this point, leading to practical consequences for all twelve scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hinge principle
The entire dispute rests on whether voluntarily exiting the prayer (al-khuruj min al-salah) is fard. Abu Hanifa holds it is fard; the Sahibayn hold it is not fard.
If it is fard, then any event before the exit occurs while the prayer is still ongoing, and thus can invalidate.
2
Understand the two positions
Abu Hanifa: exiting is fard → any event after final sitting is like an event during the prayer and invalidates (batil). Sahibayn: exiting is not fard → prayer is complete after tashahhud sitting, so events do not affect validity (tamm).
This principle applies uniformly to all twelve cases.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you have said this (tashahhud) or done this (sat), your prayer is complete; if you wish to stand, stand.' They argue this explicitly attaches completion to the tashahhud/sitting.
The phrase 'tammat salatuka' is taken literally.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa interprets 'tammat' as 'qaribat al-tamam' (close to completion) because exiting is still fard, so full completion has not occurred. The hadith does not address new impediments arising after the sitting.
This interpretation preserves the fard status of the exit.
5
Apply to the twelve cases
Review each of the twelve events (seeing water after tayammum, wiping period ending, removing khuffs, etc.) and confirm that the ruling (invalid vs valid) flows consistently from the respective principle.
The cases are all treated similarly because the difference is foundational, not case-specific.

Source Text

فان رآه بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد او كان ماسحا فانقضت مدة مسحه او خلع خفيه بعمل يسير او كان فتعلم سورة او عريانا فوجد ثوبا أو مؤميا فقدر على الركوع والسجود او تذكر فائتة عليه قبل هذا احدث الامام القارى فاستخلف اميا او طلعت الشمس فى الفجر او دخل وقت العصر وهو في الحد او كان ماسحا على الجبيرة فسقطت عن برء او كان صاحب عذر فانقطع عذره كالمستحاضة ومن بعد بطلت الصلوة في قول بى حنيفة وقالا تمت صلوته، وقيل الاصل فيه ان الخروج عن الصلوة المصلى فرض عند ابي حنيفة و ليس بفرض عندهما فاعتراض هذه العوارض عنده في هذه الح كاعتراضها في خلال الصلوة وعندهما كاعتراضها بعد التسليم لهما ما روينا من حديث ابن مسعود را لا يمكنه أداء صلوة اخرى الا بالخروج من هذه وما لا يتوصل الى الفرض الا به يكون فرضا و معنى تمت قاربت التمام والاستخلاف ليس بمفسد حتى يجوز فى حق القارى وانما الفساد ضرورة حكم شي وهو عدم صلاحية الامامة

ترجمہ اور اگر تیم نے تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد پانی دیکھا یا موزہ پر مسح کرنے والا تھا پس اس کے مسح کی مدت گذرگئی یا اپنے موزے نکالے خفیف عمل کے ساتھ یا امی تھا پس اس نے کوئی سورت سیکھ لی یا نگا تھا پس اس نے کپڑا پایا یا اشارہ سے رکوع اور سجدہ والا تھا پھر رکوع اور سجدے پر قادر ہو گیا یا یاد کیا فائنہ کو جو اس پر اس نماز سے پہلے واجب القضاء ہے یا امام قاری کو حدث ہوائیس " امی کو خلیفہ بنا دیا یا نجبر میں آفتاب طلوع ہو گیا۔ یا داخل ہو گیا عصر کا وقت در انحالیکہ وہ نماز جمعہ میں ہے یا وہ جبیرہ پر مسح کرنے والا نے اچھا ہو کر گر پڑایا وہ معذور تھا اس کا عذر منقطع ہو گیا جیسے متخاصہ عورت اور جو شخص اس کے معنی میں ہو تو ابو حنیفہ کے قول کے مطابق نماز باطل ہو گئی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اس کی نماز پوری ہو گئی ۔ کہا گیا ہے کہ اس باب میں اصل یہ ہے کہ نماز سے باہر ہونا معلمی اختیاری فعل سے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک فرض ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک فرض نہیں ہے۔ پس امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس حالت عوارض کا پیش آنا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ درمیان صلوة ان عوارض کا پیش آنا ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جیسا کہ سلام کے بعد ان عوارض کے ہے۔ کہ نمازی کے لئے دوسری نماز ادا کر ناممکن نہیں مگر اس نماز سے نکل کر اور جو چیز ایسی ہو کہ اس کے بغیر فرض تک نہ پہنچ سکتا ہوں فرض ہوگی۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول و تمت کے معنی قاربت التمام کے ہیں اور خلیفہ بنانا مفسد نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ قاری کے حق پر ہوگا اور نماز کے فساد کا حکم فقط حکم شرعی کی وجہ سے ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ امام میں امامت کی صلاحت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں مسائل اثنا عشرہ کا نام ہے یعنی ان بارہ مسائل کا بیان ہے جو تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد پیش آئیں، 1) تیم کرنے والے مصلی نے مقدار تشہد بیٹھنے کے بعد پانی دیکھا۔
(۲) یا موزوں پر مسح کرنے والا تھا پس مقدار تشہد بیٹھنے کے بعد مدت مسح پوری ہو گئی۔ (۳) یا مقدار تشہد کے بعد عمل قلیل کے ساتھ دونوں موزے نکالے یا دونوں موزوں میں سے کوئی موزہ نکالا اور عمل قلیل یہ ہے کہ و

کوشش کے اس کو یاد ہو گیا۔

یا مصلی اشارے سے رکوع اور سجدہ کرنے والا تھا پھر وہ مقدار تشہد کے بعد رکوع اور سجدہ پر قادر ہو گیا۔

) یا مصلی جبیرہ پر مسح کئے ہوئے تھا پس مقدار تشہد کے بعد اچھا ہونے سے گر پڑا۔
(۱۲) یا معذور تھا لیکن مقدار تشہد کے بعد اس کا عذر منقطع ہو گیا یعنی وہ عذر ہی جاتا رہا جیسے مستحاضہ عورت یا جو اس کے معنی میں ہو جیسے جس آدمی کو پیشاب جاری ہونے یا نکسیر جاری ہونے کا عذر ہو۔
ان بارہ مسائل میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز باطل ہوگئی اور صاحبین نے کہا ان تمام صورتوں میں نماز پوری ہوگئی ۔ بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ اس باب میں اصل یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز سے باہر ہونا مصلی کے اختیاری فعل سے فرص ہے ۔ صاحبین کے نزد یک فرض نہیں ہے۔ پس اس اصل کے پیش نظر امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کا پیش آنا جو ہر مسئلہ میں الگ الگ مذکور ہوئے ہیں ایسا ہے جیسے درمیان نماز میں پیش آنا اور چونکہ درمیان نماز ان عوارض کا پیش آنا مفسد نماز ہے اس لئے قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد بھی اگر یہ عوارض پیش آگئے تو نماز باطل ہو جائے گی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کا پیش آنا ایسا ہے جیسے سلام پھیر نے کے بعد پیش آنا اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ سلام پھیرنے کے بعد کوئی عارض نماز کو فاسد نہیں کرتا۔ اس لئے قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کے پیش آنے سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ۔
صاحبین کی دلیل عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث ہے حدیث یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابن مسعود سے فرمایا۔ اذا قلت هذا اوفعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك ان شئت ان تقوم فقم ، یعنی جب تو نے یہ کہا یا یہ کیا تو تیری نماز پوری ہوگئی اگر تیرا جی اٹھنے کو چاہتے تو تو اٹھ کھڑ اہو اس حدیث سے استدلال اس طور پر ہو گا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز پوری ہونے کو تشہد پڑھنے یا تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے پر معلق کیا ہے پس جس شخص نے تمام کو نماز کو تیسری چیز پر معلق کیا اس نے نص کی مخالفت کی۔ حاصل یہ کہ ان مسائل میں قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان
If he sees water after he sat for the amount of tashahhud, or he was a mas-h (wiping) and the period of his wiping ended, or he removed his leather socks with a slight action, or he was illiterate and then learned a surah, or he was naked and found a garment, or he was gesturing and became able to bow and prostrate, or he remembered an obligatory missed prayer that was due before this prayer, or the imam who was a qari had an event (hadath) and appointed an illiterate person as substitute, or the sun rose during Fajr prayer, or the time of Asr entered while he was in Friday prayer, or he was wiping over a splint and it fell off due to healing, or he was a person with an excuse and his excuse ended, like a mustahada woman and one after. Then the prayer is invalid in the saying of Abu Hanifa, and they (the two companions) said his prayer is complete. And it is said the basis of this is that exiting the prayer for the praying person is obligatory (fard) according to Abu Hanifa and is not obligatory according to them. So the occurrence of these impediments according to him in this case is like their occurrence during the prayer, and according to them it is like their occurrence after the taslim. For them, we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'He cannot perform another prayer except by exiting this one, and whatever is indispensable for reaching the obligatory becomes obligatory.' And the meaning of 'tammat' is 'qarabat al-tamam' (close to completion). And appointing a substitute is not invalidating, as it is valid for the qari. Invalidity only occurs due to a necessary Shar'i ruling, which is the lack of qualification for imamate.

[Urdu translation and commentary follow: explication of the twelve cases, repeating the scenarios and the dispute, affirming Abu Hanifa's view invalidates and Sahibayn's view completes. It states the underlying principle: exiting prayer voluntarily is fard for Abu Hanifa, not for Sahibayn. It then provides the proof: hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet said 'When you have said this or done this, your prayer is complete; if you wish to stand up, stand up.' The implication is that prayer completion is tied to tashahhud, so any later event does not invalidate. Abu Hanifa interprets 'complete' as 'close to completion.' The rest explains that the twelve cases are all treated similarly.]
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents a set of twelve specific events that may occur after the final tashahhud (i.e., after sitting for the amount of time it takes to recite the tashahhud) in prayer. The core issue is whether these events invalidate the prayer (i.e., require repetition) or leave it valid and complete. The text provides the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, who rules that in all such cases the prayer is invalid (batil), and the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), who rule that the prayer remains complete and valid (tamm). 

The underlying legal principle (asl) is identified: according to Abu Hanifa, the act of exiting the prayer (al-khuruj min al-salah) through one's own voluntary action is fard (obligatory) for the validity of prayer, whereas according to the Sahibayn it is not fard. Consequently, for Abu Hanifa, any event that occurs after the final sitting but before the intended exit is treated as occurring within the prayer itself and thus invalidates it. For the Sahibayn, these events occur after the prayer is effectively complete (since the final sitting is the last integral), so they are like events after the taslim and do not affect the prayer's validity.

The Sahibayn support their position with the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you have said this (the tashahhud) or done this (the final sitting), your prayer is complete; if you wish to stand up, stand up.' The Sahibayn argue that this text attaches completion to the tashahhud or the sitting, so no later act can invalidate. Abu Hanifa responds by interpreting the word 'tammat' (complete) as 'qarabat al-tamam' (close to completion) rather than actual full completion. He also notes that the hadith does not address the occurrence of new impediments after the sitting.

The twelve cases enumerated are: (1) a person performing tayammum sees water; (2) a person wiping over khuffs has the wiping period expire; (3) removes khuffs with a slight action; (4) an illiterate person (ummi) learns a surah; (5) a naked person finds a garment; (6) a person gesturing (mu'mi) becomes able to bow and prostrate; (7) remembers an earlier missed obligatory prayer; (8) the imam who is a qari (can recite well) has an event (hadath) and appoints an ummi as substitute; (9) the sun rises during Fajr; (10) the time of Asr enters while one is in Friday prayer; (11) a person wiping over a splint (jabirah) has it fall off due to healing; (12) a person with a chronic excuse (e.g., mustahada) has that excuse end.

The passage also clarifies that the act of appointing a substitute imam (istikhlaf) is not in itself invalidating; it is permissible for a qari to appoint an ummi, and the invalidity arises only because the ummi lacks the qualification for imamate in that context.

In summary, the dispute rests on whether the final sitting marks actual completion of the prayer or merely readiness for exit. This difference has practical consequences in all twelve scenarios.

Key Terms
قعد قدر التشهد (qa‘ada qadr al-tashahhud): Sitting for the amount of time it takes to recite the complete tashahhud (attestation of faith) in the final sitting of prayer.
تمت (tammat): Literally 'it is complete.' In this context, the Sahibayn interpret it as actual completion of the prayer. Abu Hanifa interprets it as 'close to completion' (قاربت التمام).
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaf): The act of an imam appointing another person to lead the remainder of the prayer due to a valid excuse (e.g., hadath).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the underlying principle that leads to the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the twelve events?
A) Whether tayammum is valid after seeing water.
B) Whether exiting the prayer (khuruj) is fard or not.
C) Whether the imam must be a qari.
D) Whether the sun rising during Fajr invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The difference in ruling on events after the final tashahhud stems from one foundational principle: whether exiting the prayer voluntarily is fard or not.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Prayer Invalidity After Final Tashahhud: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer invalidity after final tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether prayer becomes invalid due to certain incidents after the final tashahhud, and state the proof and response of each side.

Core Idea
Even after the final tashahhud, until the salam, the prayer continues – exiting is fard, so events still invalidate.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Does the prayer remain vulnerable to invalidation after the final tashahhud? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, because exiting the prayer is a fard obligation; the Sahibayn say no, citing a hadith that declares the prayer complete at that point. We will walk through the twelve example scenarios, the proofs from both sides, and the Hanafi interpretation of the key hadith.

Guided Path
1
1. List the twelve scenarios
Familiarize yourself with the range of events that can occur after the final tashahhud: from a sock falling off to learning a surah, becoming able to bow, remembering a missed prayer, etc. These scenarios set the stage for the dispute.
The first three cases are missing due to a page break; the list starts from case 4.
2
2. Identify the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in all twelve cases, the prayer becomes invalid (batil). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the prayer is complete and valid (sahih).
This is an intra-madhhab difference: both views are recorded in the zahir al-riwayah.
3
3. Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that exiting the prayer is fard because it is a means (muqawwim) to perform the next fard prayer. Since the salam has not been said, the prayer continues, and any invalidating event (like hadath) that occurs during the prayer nullifies it.
He uses a qiyas: the means to a fard is itself fard, similar to earning for nafaqah or moving from ruku' for sajdah.
4
4. Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'When you have said this and done this, your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand.' The final tashahhud marks completion; subsequent events do not affect the prayer.
This is a nass (text) that appears to contradict Abu Hanifa's position.
5
5. Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's response is not to reject the hadith but to interpret 'tammat' as 'near completion' (qaribat al-tamam), analogous to the Prophet's statement about Hajj: 'Your Hajj is complete' after Arafat, even though the circumambulation of ifadah remains obligatory.
This interpretive move (ta'wil) preserves both the hadith and the principle that salam is required for true exit.

(۸) یا مقدار تشہد کے بعد امام قاری کو حدث ہوا بس اس نے امی کو خلیفہ کر دیا۔
۹) یا مقدار تشہد کے بعد فجر کی نماز میں آفتاب طلوع ہو گیا۔
۱۰) یا مقدار تشہد کے بعد عصر کا وقت داخل ہو گیا حالانکہ یہ شخص نماز جمعہ میں ہے۔
) یا مصلی جبیرہ پر مسح کئے ہوئے تھا پس مقدار تشہد کے بعد اچھا ہونے سے گر پڑا۔
(۱۲) یا معذور تھا لیکن مقدار تشہد کے بعد اس کا عذر منقطع ہو گیا یعنی وہ عذر ہی جاتا رہا جیسے مستحاضہ عورت یا جو اس کے معنی میں ہو جیسے جس آدمی کو پیشاب جاری ہونے یا نکسیر جاری ہونے کا عذر ہو۔

ان بارہ مسائل میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز باطل ہوگئی اور صاحبین نے کہا ان تمام صورتوں میں نماز پوری ہوگئی ۔ بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ اس باب میں اصل یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز سے باہر ہونا مصلی کے اختیاری فعل سے فرص ہے ۔ صاحبین کے نزد یک فرض نہیں ہے۔ پس اس اصل کے پیش نظر امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کا پیش آنا جو ہر مسئلہ میں الگ الگ مذکور ہوئے ہیں ایسا ہے جیسے درمیان نماز میں پیش آنا اور چونکہ درمیان نماز ان عوارض کا پیش آنا مفسد نماز ہے اس لئے قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد بھی اگر یہ عوارض پیش آگئے تو نماز باطل ہو جائے گی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کا پیش آنا ایسا ہے جیسے سلام پھیر نے کے بعد پیش آنا اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ سلام پھیرنے کے بعد کوئی عارض نماز کو فاسد نہیں کرتا۔ اس لئے قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کے پیش آنے سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ۔

صاحبین کی دلیل عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث ہے حدیث یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابن مسعود سے فرمایا۔ اذا قلت هذا اوفعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك ان شئت ان تقوم فقم ، یعنی جب تو نے یہ کہا یا یہ کیا تو تیری نماز پوری ہوگئی اگر تیرا جی اٹھنے کو چاہتے تو تو اٹھ کھڑ اہو اس حدیث سے استدلال اس طور پر ہو گا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز پوری ہونے کو تشہد پڑھنے یا تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے پر معلق کیا ہے پس جس شخص نے تمام کو نماز کو تیسری چیز پر معلق کیا اس نے نص کی مخالفت کی۔ حاصل یہ کہ ان مسائل میں قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد ان عوارض کا ذکر ہے اور قعدہ اخیر و پر نماز پوری ہوگئی پس جب قعدہ اخیرہ پر نماز پوری ہوگئی تو اس کے بعد نماز باطل ہونے کا کیا سوال ہے امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دوسری نماز کا اس کے وقت میں ادا کرنا فرض ہے اور ممکن نہیں ہو گا کہ جب تک اس موجود ہ نہیں ہا ہر نہ ہو۔ پس اس موجودہ نماز سے نکلنا دوسری فرض نماز ادا کرنے کا ذریعہ ہے یعنی دوسری فرض نماز ادا کرنا اس موجودہ نماز سے کے موقوف ہے۔ اور چونکہ فرض کا موقوف علیہ بھی فرض ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس موجودہ نماز سے نکلنا بھی فرض ہوگا یہی وجہ ہے کہ امام ابم کے نزدیک خروج بصدقہ فرض ہے۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص پر نفقہ واجب ہے اور وہ بغیر کمائی کئے حاصل نہیں ہوسکتا تواس پر کالی فرض کا موقوف عالیہ بھی فرض ہوتا ہے۔ بھی فرض ہوگا ۔ یا مثلا سجدہ فرض ہے اور یہ اس وقت تک ممکن نہیں جب تک کہ رکوع سے منتقل نہ ہو پس یہ منتقل ہونا بھی فرض ہوگا ۔ 

و معنى قوله تمت الج سے حدیث ابن مسعود کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں قسمت صلو تک ۔ قاربت التمام کے ہیں یعنی جب تو نے یہ کہ لیایا یہ کرلیا تو تیری نماز تمام ہونے کے قریب ہو گئی یہ ایسا ہے جیسا کہ حضور کا قول وقف بعرفته فقدتم حجه، یعنی جس نے وقوف عرفہ کیا اس کا حج تام ہو گیا حالانکہ وقوف عرفہ کے بعد ابھی طواف زیارت کا فرش رہتا ہے پس یہاں بھی یہی معنی ہوں گے کہ اس کا حج تمام ہونے کے قریب ہو گیا۔
Chapter of Hadath in Prayer. Similarly, [from the list] such that there was no need for hands, only by pointing the foot a sock came off. (4) Or the prayer was illiterate, then after sitting the amount of tashahhud he learned a surah of the Quran. The author of al-Inayah said the meaning is that he had forgotten the Quran but after the amount of tashahhud he remembered; it does not mean he studied because studying requires teaching and teaching is an action contrary to prayer... (then lists cases 5-12) In these twelve issues, according to Imam Abu Hanifa the prayer becomes invalid, and the Sahibayn said in all these situations the prayer is complete... The proof of the Sahibayn is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud... The proof of Abu Hanifa is that performing the next prayer in its time is fard, and it is not possible until he exits this prayer; thus exiting becomes fard... The response to the hadith is that the word 'tammat' in the hadith means 'near completion' as in the hadith of Hajj...
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether certain incidents after the final tashahhud invalidate the prayer. The text lists twelve scenarios (starting from case 4 due to page cuts) where an event occurs after sitting for the final tashahhud. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer becomes invalid because exiting the prayer is fard (obligatory) to perform the next prayer, and until the salam, the prayer is still in progress, so these events nullify it. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the final tashahhud completes the prayer, as per the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and subsequent events do not affect it. The author then provides Abu Hanifa's rational proof (qiyas) that the means to a fard is itself fard, similar to how earning is fard for one who must provide nafaqah, or moving from ruku' is fard for performing sajdah. The response to the Sahibayn's hadith interprets 'tammat' as 'near completion' (qaribat al-tamam), analogous to the Prophet's statement about Hajj where 'your Hajj is complete' after Arafat but the remaining rites are still required. The thamarah al-khilaf is that Abu Hanifa requires the prayer to be repeated, while the Sahibayn consider it valid.

Key Terms
قعدہ اخیرہ (qa‘dah akhīrah): The final sitting in prayer after the last sajdah, during which one recites the tashahhud and other supplications.
تشہد (tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (at-tahiyyāt) during the sitting in prayer.
صاحبین (sāhibayn): The two leading disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the Sahibayn's primary evidence for considering the prayer complete after the final tashahhud?
A) Qiyas on the obligation of salam
B) Hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud
C) The principle that the final tashahhud is a rukn
D) The consensus of the Hanafi school

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, whether events after the final tashahhud invalidate the prayer depends on whether one views the prayer as still ongoing (Abu Hanifa) or complete (Sahibayn) — a key intra-madhab difference with practical consequences.
